# Plan Command

Plan a new feature or task with proper structure before implementation.

**Reference skills based on feature type:**
- API/backend: Read `.claude/skills/api-design-patterns/SKILL.md`
- React components: Read `.claude/skills/react-patterns/SKILL.md`
- UI styling: Read `.claude/skills/tailwind-conventions/SKILL.md`
- Error handling: Read `.claude/skills/error-handler/SKILL.md`
- TDD mode: Read `.claude/skills/test-generator/SKILL.md`

**For new projects:** Use `/greenfield` first to define specs, then `/plan` for implementation.

## Flags

- `--tdd` - Enable Test-Driven Development mode (write tests first)

## Validation

If no feature description provided, ask for one.

## Planning Steps

### 1. Gather Context (REQUIRED)

**You MUST read relevant files before creating a plan.** Don't plan based on assumptions.

Before planning:
- Read relevant CLAUDE.md files
- **Read the actual files** that will be modified
- Identify existing patterns and conventions
- Understand related code and dependencies

Use `Explore` agent or direct file reads to understand:
- Current implementation
- Existing patterns in similar code
- Test file locations and patterns

### 2. Requirements Clarification

Ask clarifying questions if needed:
- What is the expected behavior?
- What are the edge cases?
- What are the acceptance criteria?
- Are there performance requirements?

### 3. Create Plan

Structure the implementation with **specific details**:

**Detail Level Guidelines:**

| Change Type | Detail Level |
|-------------|--------------|
| Complex/risky changes | Line numbers + code snippets |
| Medium changes | Function/method names |
| Simple/obvious changes | File paths only |
| New files | File path + structure outline |

**Output Format:**
```
## Feature: [description]

### Requirements
- [ ] Requirement 1
- [ ] Requirement 2

### Technical Approach
1. Step 1 - [description]
   - Why: [reasoning for this approach]
2. Step 2 - [description]

### Files to Modify

#### `path/to/file.ts` (lines 45-67)
**Current:** [brief description of current state]
**Change:** [what will change]
```typescript
// Example of the change (for complex modifications)
function existingFunction() {
  // Add: new caching logic here
}
```

#### `path/to/new-file.ts` (NEW)
**Purpose:** [why this file is needed]
**Structure:**
- `functionA()` - [purpose]
- `functionB()` - [purpose]

### Dependencies
- [list any new dependencies]

### Testing Strategy
- Unit tests: [specific test cases]
- Integration tests: [approach]
- Test file: `path/to/tests/file.test.ts`

### Alternatives Considered
- [Alternative 1] - [why not chosen]

### Risks
- [potential issue] - [mitigation]

### Complexity
- [low/medium/high] - [justification]
```

### 4. TDD Mode (if --tdd flag)

When `--tdd` is specified, modify the plan to include:

```
### TDD Implementation Order

1. **Acceptance Criteria → Test Cases**
   - [ ] Test: [criteria 1 as test]
   - [ ] Test: [criteria 2 as test]

2. **Write Failing Tests First**
   Files to create/modify:
   - `__tests__/feature.test.ts` - [test descriptions]

3. **Implement to Pass Tests**
   - Implement minimum code to pass each test
   - Run tests after each change

4. **Refactor**
   - Clean up while keeping tests green
```

**TDD Workflow:**
```
Write test → Run (FAIL) → Implement → Run (PASS) → Refactor → Run (PASS)
```

### 5. Confidence Check

Run Pre-Implementation Confidence Check before proceeding.

### 6. Await Approval

Present plan and wait for user approval before implementation.

**Key review points for user:**
- Are the file changes correct?
- Is the approach sound?
- Any concerns about the changes?

## Example (Standard)

```
## Feature: Add rate limiting to API

### Requirements
- [ ] Limit requests to 100/minute per user
- [ ] Return 429 when exceeded
- [ ] Log rate limit hits

### Technical Approach
1. Add rate limiting middleware using existing Express pattern
   - Why: Consistent with authMiddleware.ts approach
2. Store counters in Redis (already used for sessions)

### Files to Modify

#### `src/middleware/rateLimitMiddleware.ts` (NEW)
**Purpose:** Rate limiting middleware
**Structure:**
- `rateLimiter()` - Express middleware
- `getRateKey()` - Generate Redis key

#### `src/app.ts` (line 23)
**Current:** Auth middleware only
**Change:** Add rate limiter after auth
```typescript
app.use(authMiddleware);
app.use(rateLimiter({ limit: 100, window: 60 })); // ADD
```

### Testing Strategy
- Unit tests: Mock Redis, test limit logic
- Integration tests: Hit endpoint 101 times
- Test file: `__tests__/middleware/rateLimitMiddleware.test.ts`

### Alternatives Considered
- express-rate-limit package - Adds dependency, we can do simpler

### Risks
- Redis connection issues - Fail open (allow requests)

### Complexity
- Medium - New middleware but follows existing patterns
```

## Example (TDD Mode)

```
/plan --tdd Add rate limiting to API
```

```
## Feature: Add rate limiting to API (TDD)

### TDD Implementation Order

1. **Acceptance Criteria → Test Cases**
   - [ ] Test: Returns 200 for requests under limit
   - [ ] Test: Returns 429 when limit exceeded
   - [ ] Test: Resets after window expires
   - [ ] Test: Different users have separate limits

2. **Write Failing Tests First**
   File: `__tests__/middleware/rateLimitMiddleware.test.ts`
   ```typescript
   describe('rateLimiter', () => {
     it('allows requests under limit', async () => { ... });
     it('returns 429 when limit exceeded', async () => { ... });
     it('resets after window expires', async () => { ... });
   });
   ```

3. **Implement to Pass Tests**
   - Create `rateLimitMiddleware.ts`
   - Implement `rateLimiter()` function
   - Run tests after each addition

4. **Refactor**
   - Extract Redis key generation
   - Add JSDoc comments
```

## Next Steps

After approval:
- If `--tdd`: Write tests first, then implement
- Otherwise: Start implementation
- Use `/review` for code review
- Use `/validate` to verify before completion
- Use `/ship` when ready to commit

Base directory for this skill: /home/ubuntu/.claude/skills/code-writing-guidelines

## Code should read like prose
Anyone with moderate software development proficiency should be able to understand how our code works. This DOES NOT mean that we flood our code with docstrings and comments. That would be like reading a book where all the interesting content was contained in the footnotes. Our code should tell a story. You do this by implementing the following strategies:
1. Use descriptive function names and variable names — including locals with small scope. `s` is not acceptable when `samples` is clearer. The only exception is standard mathematical notation (e.g., EKF matrices F, P, H, K, state vectors x, y).
2. Create linear data flows.
3. Be efficient, in terms of how many lines of code you write.
4. Keep the code DRY.
5. Do not mix concerns. Functions should perform ONE primary task. A class should have ONE primary purpose. A directory should have ONE common theme.
6. Check your work. If you're confused, then someone else with even less context will definitely be confused.
7. Use the principles of TDD without necessarily writing tests all the time. All code should be testable, even if we don't have a test for it.
8. Always use curly braces for `if`, `else`, `for`, `while`, even for single-line bodies. clang-format will not add them — this is enforced by discipline and clang-tidy review.
9. Never put multiple statements on a single line.

## Always make it better
Whenever we touch code, we have a chance to improve it. We never take the attitude of "that wasn't our change, so we don't touch it". We are a small team, with zero customers. We can make breaking changes at any time. This does not mean that we are reckless. Don't change the code until you truly understand how it works. If you think that there is an opportunity for improvement that is our of scope for the current change, then add an entry to BACKLOG.md.

## If you find a bug, write a test first
Every bug we find, means that we had a failure in test coverage. Before you fix a bug, find a way to write a test that uncovers the bug. If you can't write a test for it, that means that we need to refactor the code first.
1. If you can't trigger a bug with a test, refactor until you can.
2. Write a test that uncovers the bug.
3. Fix the bug.

But before you get carried away, read the next section

## Remove tests as we go
Imagine the following scenario:
- We have a class, BigClass, with functions A(), B(), and C()
- We write tests to call A(), B(), and C()
- We then add function D(), which calls A(), B(), and C()
- We write a test to call D()

We can then remove the tests for A(), B(), and C(), as they are implicitly called by the D() test, ASSUMING that these tests are duplicated by the D() test. Keep any tests that are not covered by regular operation.

## Trace the data before writing the code
No piece of code exists in isolation. Before writing or modifying a function, trace the data it touches — where does it come from, what constraints does it already carry, and what does every downstream consumer expect? When you follow data through the system, you will find redundant conversions, mismatched types, unnecessary validation, and missing abstractions. The right design becomes obvious when you understand the full journey of the data, not just the local function.

## Make invalid states unrepresentable
When a value has constraints — a valid range, a fixed set of options, a non-null requirement — encode those constraints in the type. If bad data can't be constructed, you don't need code to check for it. This eliminates scattered validation, defensive checks, and the bugs that happen when someone forgets one.

## Don't reinvent the wheel
None of our individual functions, classes, or modules are performing tasks that haven't been done before. We are inventing something by combining logic in new ways. We don't need create all of our code from scratch. Whenever possible, let's benefit from any knowledge base that we can. We should explore multiple ways of accomplishing our tasks. You are an expert in code implementation. I can an expert in invention, creativity, and aerosapce applications. Leverage open source software for code strategies, and leverage me for interpreting these strategies and finding new ways to apply them.

# Code Review

Review all changes on the current branch against main.

## Process

### 1. Gather Changes

```bash
git diff main --name-only
```

If no changes, inform the user and stop.

For each changed file, read the FULL file (not just the diff) to understand context. Also run:

```bash
git diff main
```

### 2. Review Against Guidelines

#### Code Reads Like Prose
- Descriptive function and variable names — no abbreviations that require mental decoding
- Linear data flows — can you read top-to-bottom without jumping around?
- Efficient line count — no bloat, no unnecessary abstractions
- DRY — is anything duplicated that shouldn't be?
- Single responsibility — each function does ONE thing, each class has ONE purpose
- Testable — could you write a test for this without mocking half the system?

#### Make Invalid States Unrepresentable
- Constraints encoded in types, not runtime checks
- No scattered validation for the same invariant
- `std::optional`, enums, and constructors used to enforce validity

#### Trace the Data
- Where does each value come from? What constraints does it carry?
- Are there redundant conversions or unnecessary intermediates?
- Does every downstream consumer get what it expects?

#### Always Make It Better
- Did we touch code without improving it?
- Are there obvious improvements just outside the diff boundary? (note in suggestions, don't block)

#### Project Conventions (from CLAUDE.md)
- No docstrings unless asked
- No fallbacks — code works or fails loudly
- No dead code, no commented-out experiments
- No default arguments
- Leading underscores for class data members
- PascalCase functions, snake_case locals, kCamelCase constants
- "latest" not "last" for most recent values
- Parameter passing: pointer for mutation, const ref for read-only, const value for scalars

### 3. Check For Slop
- Comments that explain "what" instead of "why"
- Defensive checks for conditions that can't happen
- Unnecessary try/catch or error handling beyond system boundaries
- Verbose logging that doesn't match existing patterns
- Style inconsistencies with surrounding code

### 4. Present Results

```
## Review Summary

**Assessment**: [APPROVE / REQUEST CHANGES]

### Positive Findings
- What was done well

### Required Changes
- Issues that must be fixed (file:line references)

### Suggestions
- Optional improvements

### Convention Violations
- Any CLAUDE.md or guideline violations
```

Be specific with file:line references. Prioritize correctness and readability over micro-optimizations. If approved, suggest running `/validate-smol` next.

Code Review: copperpunk/dubins — Initial Commit

Files reviewed: types.h, math_utils.h, circle.h, planner.h, follower.h, manager.h
🔴 Critical
1. TurnDir enum names are reversed (circle.h, follower.h)

Files: dubins/types.h, dubins/circle.h, dubins/follower.h

The geographic meaning of kRight and kLeft is inverted.

ComputeCircleCenter uses chi + lambda * π/2. With lambda=−1 (kRight), heading north (chi=0), the center lands at angle −π/2 from the north axis, which is west in (x=north, y=east) — that's the vehicle's left side. Confirmable via FollowOrbit: with lambda=−1 and bearing_from_center=0 (vehicle north of center), course_cmd = 0 + (−1)*(π/2) = −π/2 = west, so the vehicle orbits counterclockwise (geographic left). With lambda=+1 (kLeft), the course command is east and the orbit is clockwise (geographic right).

Both functions are self-consistent with each other, but the enum names are the geographic opposite of their behavior. kLeft=+1 traces clockwise (right) orbits on a map; kRight=−1 traces counterclockwise (left) orbits.

The comment in circle.h compounds the confusion:
C++

// Right turn (lambda=-1): center is 90 deg clockwise from course

"90° clockwise from course" on a map is east (when heading north), but the formula produces west.

The comment in types.h also disagrees with the formula: kRight = -1 is labelled "Right" but produces left geographic turns.

Impact: Purely cosmetic for the shortest-path selection (all 6 types are tried), but behaviorally wrong for loiter direction. A caller setting loiter_dir = TurnDir::kRight for a standard clockwise holding pattern gets a counterclockwise orbit instead.

Fix options:

    Swap the enum values: kRight = 1, kLeft = -1 (and update all downstream lambda = static_cast<float>(dir) uses).
    Or keep the values and rename: kCcw = -1, kCw = 1 to avoid the geographic implication, then document the geographic mapping.

2. FollowOrbit double-counts helix turns, then wraps progress (follower.h, planner.h)

Two separate bugs that interact:

Bug A — double counting. In BuildSegments, a helix segment is stored as:
C++

seg->arc_span_rad = kTwoPi * static_cast<float>(helix_turns);  // = N·2π
seg->helix_turns  = helix_turns;                                 // = N

Then in FollowOrbit:
C++

float total_angle = seg.arc_span_rad + static_cast<float>(seg.helix_turns) * kTwoPi;
//                = N·2π + N·2π = 2N·2π

The total angle is doubled, so the altitude fraction at any given angular position is half what it should be.

Bug B — progress wraps every turn. angular_progress uses WrapTo2Pi(...), so its range is always [0, 2π). For a 3-turn helix the "progress" resets to zero at the start of every new lap. The Clampf(..., 0, 1) means the altitude command climbs to only 1/(2N) of the target altitude on the first lap, then resets.

Combined result: The altitude interpolation through a helix segment is wrong for any N ≥ 1.

Fix: arc_span_rad for a helix should store one full revolution (kTwoPi), not N·kTwoPi; the helix_turns field carries the lap count. Then total_angle is kTwoPi + N·kTwoPi = (N+1)·kTwoPi... but that's still wrong for tracking multi-turn progress, because WrapTo2Pi wraps the bearing. The proper fix requires either (a) tracking cumulative angular position externally in PathManager, or (b) storing the full N·kTwoPi in arc_span_rad and removing the + helix_turns·kTwoPi term in FollowOrbit — accepting that altitude interpolation will be "first-lap" only and adding a comment to that effect.
🟠 High
3. ComputeHelixTurns divides by zero when gamma_max_rad = 0 (planner.h)
C++

float dz_per_turn = circumference * tanf(gamma_max_rad);  // tanf(0) = 0
int turns = static_cast<int>(ceilf(excess_dz / dz_per_turn));  // ÷0

tanf(0) is exactly 0; ceilf(inf) or ceilf(nan) cast to int is undefined behaviour. A zero climb angle means the aircraft cannot change altitude at all; the only valid response for a non-zero dz is to return infinity (infeasible) or at minimum guard the divide.
C++

if (gamma_max_rad < 1e-9f) {
    return (fabsf(dz_m) > 1e-6f) ? INT_MAX : 0;
}

4. PlanMission silently truncates missions > 32 waypoints (planner.h)
C++

static constexpr int kMaxWaypoints = 32;
int wp_count = (count <= kMaxWaypoints) ? count : kMaxWaypoints;

The function signature accepts int count without bound, but silently processes at most 32 waypoints and returns a leg_count smaller than count − 1 without any indication of truncation. A caller with 40 waypoints gets 31 legs with no warning, not 39.

Either document the limit clearly in the function signature (and have callers assert it), or return −1 / some sentinel when the limit is exceeded.
🟡 Medium
5. FnvHash is undefined behaviour under strict aliasing (types.h)
C++

inline uint32_t FnvHash(uint32_t hash, const int32_t value) {
  auto bytes = reinterpret_cast<const uint8_t*>(&value);
  for (int i = 0; i < 4; ++i) { ... }
}

Casting int32_t* to uint8_t* and reading through it is technically UB under the C++ strict aliasing rule (only char*, unsigned char*, and std::byte* are aliasing-safe). Practically GCC/Clang pass on embedded targets, but it is flagged by -fsanitize=undefined and std::byte or memcpy are the standard fixes:
C++

uint8_t bytes[4];
std::memcpy(bytes, &value, 4);

6. QuantizeMeters and QuantizeRadians are identical functions (types.h)
C++

inline int32_t QuantizeMeters(const float value)  { return static_cast<int32_t>(roundf(value * 1000.0f)); }
inline int32_t QuantizeRadians(const float value) { return static_cast<int32_t>(roundf(value * 1000.0f)); }

Identical bodies imply they could diverge intentionally (e.g., different precision for positions vs. angles), but they never do. A reader or future maintainer looking at ComputePathDigest will assume the scales differ when they don't. Consider merging them into a single Quantize helper and making the intent explicit, or add a comment explaining the equal precision is deliberate.
7. Line segments hash uninitialised/zero direction field (types.h, planner.h)

ComputePathDigest hashes seg.direction unconditionally for all segment types:
C++

hash = digest::FnvHash(hash, static_cast<int32_t>(seg.direction));

For kLine segments, direction is never set by BuildSegments (see lines 365–393). The field happens to be 0 (from DubinsPath best = {} zero-init) which is neither kRight(−1) nor kLeft(1) — a sentinel that the enum doesn't define. The hash is deterministic only because of zero-init, which is fragile. Either skip hashing direction for line segments, or explicitly set it (e.g., to a neutral value or the preceding arc's direction).
🔵 Low / Style
8. WrapToPi can return −π for input exactly +π (math_utils.h)
C++

float r = fmodf(rad + kPi, kTwoPi);
return r <= 0.0f ? r + kPi : r - kPi;

For rad = π: fmodf(2π, 2π) should be 0, but floating-point rounding may give a tiny positive ε. Then r > 0 → r − π ≈ −π, which is the excluded end of the (−π, π] range. This is the same ULP hazard already documented in PLAN.md for ArcSpan. The fix is the same pattern: if |r - 2π| < ε, clamp to 0 before the branch.
9. FollowSegment altitude_m parameter unused in normal path (follower.h)
C++

inline FollowerOutput FollowSegment(const float north_m, const float east_m,
                                    const float altitude_m,   // ← only used in unreachable fallthrough
                                    const PathSegment& seg,
                                    const FollowerParams& params)

altitude_m is only used in the unreachable return after the switch. FollowLine and FollowOrbit both derive their altitude from the segment's z_start_m/z_end_m. The parameter exists but is a silent no-op, which is confusing. Add [[maybe_unused]] or remove the parameter and change the fallthrough return to use a fixed fallback (e.g., seg.z_start_m).
10. Non-loiter legs leave loiter_center/loiter_dir uninitialised (planner.h)
C++

} else {
    leg->has_loiter = false;
    leg->loiter_radius_m = 0.0f;
    leg->loiter_time_s = 0.0f;
    // loiter_center and loiter_dir are NOT cleared
}

If legs_out is stack memory, loiter_center and loiter_dir will contain garbage when has_loiter == false. ComputeLegDigest guards on has_loiter, so the digest is safe — but a reader printing or inspecting the struct will see misleading values. Zero the whole leg at the start of the loop iteration, or explicitly clear loiter_center = {} and loiter_dir.
11. PathManager::SetPath accepts invalid DubinsPath silently (manager.h)

If path.valid == false (e.g., start == end at degenerate geometry), SetPath still transitions to kFollowingPath with segment_count = 0. The first Update call immediately calls AdvanceSegment (since CrossedHalfPlane on a zeroed segment is trivially true), which would transition to kComplete or kLoitering in the same tick. This is arguably harmless, but an early guard (if (!path.valid) { Reset(); return; }) would make the intent explicit.
12. kMaxWaypoints is a static constexpr local — multi-TU concerns (planner.h)

static constexpr int kMaxWaypoints = 32 inside an inline function body is fine for a single-file header library, but the static keyword is redundant here (constexpr local variables are already implicitly static in C++). This is a minor style point but adds false emphasis.

Summary:
1. Primary Request and Intent:
   The user requested building Phase 3.5 of the smol flight controller — a 3D Dubins path planning and path following library as a standalone git submodule at `lib/dubins/`. Key requirements were: 3D-first design (not 2D extended to 3D), helical climbs for altitude changes, path planning and following designed together, GCS integration considered, and loiter support from the start. The library should be pure geometry/math with no HAL/MAVLink dependencies. Public API should use degrees and descriptive names; internal math uses radians. The user emphasized moving slowly and following code-writing-guidelines. The submodule is hosted at https://github.com/copperpunk/dubins.

2. Key Technical Concepts:
   - 3D Dubins airplane paths (Owen/Beard/McLain) — 6 path types (RSR, LSL, RSL, LSR, RLR, LRL) with 3 altitude cases (low/medium/high)
   - Helical climbs: extra full turns on start circle when altitude change exceeds what the 2D path can accommodate at gamma_max
   - Vector-field path following (Nelson/Barber/McLain/Beard) — saturating arctangent for line following, orbit vector field for arcs
   - Half-plane switching for segment transitions
   - Helix multi-turn position resolution using altitude + bearing (no lap counting needed, survives flight mode interruptions)
   - PathManager helix exit: requires BOTH altitude within tolerance AND half-plane crossing
   - FNV-1a quantized path digest for cross-platform verification (C++ ↔ JS)
   - Waypoints over MAVLink (MISSION_ITEM_INT), paths computed locally on both GCS and FC
   - Heading inference from waypoint sequence (NAN = auto-infer bearing to next waypoint)
   - MissionLeg pairs transit path with optional loiter at destination
   - Turn direction: kCw (+1, clockwise on map) and kCcw (-1, counterclockwise on map)
   - Public API in degrees, internal math in radians, with InternalPose as the conversion boundary
   - Header-only C++ library, no external dependencies

3. Files and Code Sections:

   - **lib/dubins/dubins/types.h** — Core public types and path digest
     - Contains: Vec2, Vec3, Pose3 (course_deg), TurnDir (kCcw/kCw), SegmentType (kHelix/kArc/kLine/kLoiter), DubinsType, PathSegment, DubinsPath, FollowerOutput (course_cmd_deg, altitude_cmd_m), FollowerParams (line_gain, orbit_gain, max_correction_deg), Waypoint (heading_deg, loiter fields), ManagerState, FNV-1a digest functions
     - Key: `digest::Quantize()` single function (was QuantizeMeters/QuantizeRadians), FnvHash uses memcpy not reinterpret_cast, ComputePathDigest skips direction for kLine segments

   - **lib/dubins/dubins/math_utils.h** — Angle math and utilities
     - Contains: kPi, kTwoPi, kHalfPi, kDegToRad, kRadToDeg, WrapTo2Pi, WrapToPi, AngleDiffRad, Dist2D, Dot2D, CrossedHalfPlane, Clampf
     - Key fix: WrapToPi uses `r <= 0.0f` (not `< 0.0f`) for correct (-pi, pi] range

   - **lib/dubins/dubins/circle.h** — Turn circle geometry
     - Contains: ComputeCircleCenter, AngleOnCircle, ArcSpan (with near-zero/near-2pi guard), ArcLength, ComputeOuterTangent (tries both tangent sides), ComputeCrossTangent, ComputeCCCGeometry
     - Key: ArcSpan guard `span < 1e-4f || span > kTwoPi - 1e-4f → 0.0f` prevents 1-ULP float artifacts
     - Key: ComputeOuterTangent takes vehicle_start_angle and vehicle_end_angle to pick shorter side

   - **lib/dubins/dubins/planner.h** — Path computation and mission planning
     - Contains: InternalPose (course_rad), ToInternal(), PathCandidate, Compute2DCandidate, Compute2DPathLength, ComputeHelixTurns (with gamma_max=0 guard returning INT_MAX), ComputeGamma, PointOnArc, CourseOnArc, SetHalfPlane, BuildSegments (with fill_altitude lambda), ComputeDubinsPath (public API, degrees), InferHeading (returns degrees), MissionLeg, ComputeLegDigest, PlanMission (returns -1 if >32 waypoints, zeros whole leg with `*leg = {}`)
     - Key: Helix stored as single segment with `seg->helix_turns = N` and `seg->arc_span_rad = N*2pi`

   - **lib/dubins/dubins/follower.h** — Vector-field path following
     - Contains: FollowLine (no altitude_m param), FollowOrbit (takes current_altitude_m for helix), FollowSegment (dispatch)
     - Key helix altitude resolution in FollowOrbit:
       ```cpp
       float dz_per_turn = total_dz / static_cast<float>(seg.helix_turns);
       float angular_within_turn = WrapTo2Pi(lambda * (bearing_from_center - seg.arc_start_rad));
       float turn_from_altitude = (current_altitude_m - seg.z_start_m) / dz_per_turn;
       float completed_turns = floorf(Clampf(turn_from_altitude, 0.0f, seg.helix_turns));
       float total_progress = completed_turns + angular_within_turn / kTwoPi;
       float fraction = Clampf(total_progress / seg.helix_turns, 0.0f, 1.0f);
       altitude_cmd = seg.z_start_m + total_dz * fraction;
       ```

   - **lib/dubins/dubins/manager.h** — PathManager FSM
     - Contains: PathManager class with Init, SetPath (guards path.valid), SetLoiter, Update, AdvanceFromLoiter, GetState, CurrentSegmentIndex, IsComplete, Reset
     - Key: Helix exit requires both altitude and half-plane:
       ```cpp
       constexpr float kHelixAltitudeToleranceM = 5.0f;
       bool altitude_ok = (seg.type != SegmentType::kHelix) ||
                          (fabsf(altitude_m - seg.z_end_m) < kHelixAltitudeToleranceM);
       ```
     - FSM: kIdle → kFollowingPath → kLoitering → kComplete

   - **lib/dubins/PLAN.md** — Strategy/progress document (no code)

   - **platformio.ini** — Added `-I lib/dubins` to native, native_sil envs; `dubins` to lib_ignore
   - **CMakeLists.txt** — Added `lib/dubins` to target_include_directories for smol_live and smol_replay

   - **test/test_dubins_math/test_dubins_math.cpp** — 41 tests (angle wrapping, circle geometry, tangents, CCC)
   - **test/test_dubins_planner/test_dubins_planner.cpp** — 42 tests (2D paths, helix turns, 3D planner, mission planning, digest)
     - Uses InternalPose with radians for internal function tests, Pose3 with degrees for public API tests
     - Has kGammaMaxRad for internal tests, kGammaMaxDeg for public API tests
   - **test/test_dubins_follower/test_dubins_follower.cpp** — 19 tests (line/orbit following, helix altitude resolution)
   - **test/test_dubins_manager/test_dubins_manager.cpp** — 10 tests (FSM, loiter, kinematic simulation)

4. Errors and fixes:
   - **ArcSpan 1-ULP float artifact**: `atan2f(25,0)` and `kHalfPi` differ by 1 ULP, causing near-zero arc spans to wrap to near-2pi via WrapTo2Pi. Fixed with dual guard: `span < 1e-4f || span > kTwoPi - 1e-4f → 0.0f`
   - **Outer tangent picks wrong side**: ComputeOuterTangent only tried one tangent line, causing straight-ahead paths to add unnecessary half-circle arcs. Fixed by trying both sides (theta ± pi/2) and picking shorter total.
   - **180-degree turn test had coincident circle centers**: Test configuration `(0, -2R)` heading south put both RSR circles at same point. Fixed test to use same-position opposite-heading.
   - **Orbit inside/outside steering test assertions reversed**: For CCW orbit with vehicle north of center, inside steers more northward (smaller chi), not larger. Fixed assertion directions.
   - **Missing kDegToRad/kRadToDeg**: After adding deg/rad conversion, these constants weren't in math_utils.h. Added them.
   - **Stale references after renames**: Multiple rounds of `chi_rad → course_rad/deg`, `gamma_rad → climb_angle_deg`, `k_path → line_gain`, etc. needed careful tracking across all files.
   - **User feedback "chi_rad doesn't make sense to API users"**: Renamed all public-facing fields to descriptive names (course_deg, heading_deg, line_gain, orbit_gain, max_correction_deg, max_climb_angle_deg, climb_angle_deg).
   - **User feedback "angles should be degrees"**: Changed all public API from radians to degrees, added InternalPose for radians boundary.
   - **User feedback on Issue #2 helix design**: Multiple iterations:
     1. Split into N segments → "Why limit the number?" 
     2. Lap counting in PathManager → "What about flight mode interruption?"
     3. Altitude-only exit → "We don't know where the aircraft is in 3D"
     4. Final: altitude + bearing resolves exact position → approved
   - **Code review Issue #1 TurnDir reversed**: kRight/kLeft geographic meaning inverted. Renamed to kCcw/kCw.
   - **Code review Issue #2 double-counting**: arc_span_rad stored N*2pi AND helix_turns*2pi added in FollowOrbit. Fixed with altitude+bearing resolution.
   - **Code review Issue #3 div by zero**: ComputeHelixTurns with gamma_max=0. Added guard returning INT_MAX.
   - **WrapToPi boundary**: `r < 0.0f` changed to `r <= 0.0f` for correct (-pi, pi] range.

5. Problem Solving:
   - Designed the complete waypoint-to-path data flow across GCS (JS), MAVLink, and FC (C++)
   - Solved the helix multi-turn position ambiguity using altitude as the disambiguator
   - Designed path digest for cross-platform verification without being brittle to float differences
   - Resolved the outer tangent side-selection problem for straight-ahead configurations
   - Handled the 1-ULP float precision issue in ArcSpan systematically

# Plan Command

Plan a new feature or task with proper structure before implementation.

**Reference skills based on feature type:**
- API/backend: Read `.claude/skills/api-design-patterns/SKILL.md`
- React components: Read `.claude/skills/react-patterns/SKILL.md`
- UI styling: Read `.claude/skills/tailwind-conventions/SKILL.md`
- Error handling: Read `.claude/skills/error-handler/SKILL.md`
- TDD mode: Read `.claude/skills/test-generator/SKILL.md`

**For new projects:** Use `/greenfield` first to define specs, then `/plan` for implementation.

## Flags

- `--tdd` - Enable Test-Driven Development mode (write tests first)

## Validation

If no feature description provided, ask for one.

## Planning Steps

### 1. Gather Context (REQUIRED)

**You MUST read relevant files before creating a plan.** Don't plan based on assumptions.

Before planning:
- Read relevant CLAUDE.md files
- **Read the actual files** that will be modified
- Identify existing patterns and conventions
- Understand related code and dependencies

Use `Explore` agent or direct file reads to understand:
- Current implementation
- Existing patterns in similar code
- Test file locations and patterns

### 2. Requirements Clarification

Ask clarifying questions if needed:
- What is the expected behavior?
- What are the edge cases?
- What are the acceptance criteria?
- Are there performance requirements?

### 3. Create Plan

Structure the implementation with **specific details**:

**Detail Level Guidelines:**

| Change Type | Detail Level |
|-------------|--------------|
| Complex/risky changes | Line numbers + code snippets |
| Medium changes | Function/method names |
| Simple/obvious changes | File paths only |
| New files | File path + structure outline |

**Output Format:**
```
## Feature: [description]

### Requirements
- [ ] Requirement 1
- [ ] Requirement 2

### Technical Approach
1. Step 1 - [description]
   - Why: [reasoning for this approach]
2. Step 2 - [description]

### Files to Modify

#### `path/to/file.ts` (lines 45-67)
**Current:** [brief description of current state]
**Change:** [what will change]
```typescript
// Example of the change (for complex modifications)
function existingFunction() {
  // Add: new caching logic here
}
```

#### `path/to/new-file.ts` (NEW)
**Purpose:** [why this file is needed]
**Structure:**
- `functionA()` - [purpose]
- `functionB()` - [purpose]

### Dependencies
- [list any new dependencies]

### Testing Strategy
- Unit tests: [specific test cases]
- Integration tests: [approach]
- Test file: `path/to/tests/file.test.ts`

### Alternatives Considered
- [Alternative 1] - [why not chosen]

### Risks
- [potential issue] - [mitigation]

### Complexity
- [low/medium/high] - [justification]
```

### 4. TDD Mode (if --tdd flag)

When `--tdd` is specified, modify the plan to include:

```
### TDD Implementation Order

1. **Acceptance Criteria → Test Cases**
   - [ ] Test: [criteria 1 as test]
   - [ ] Test: [criteria 2 as test]

2. **Write Failing Tests First**
   Files to create/modify:
   - `__tests__/feature.test.ts` - [test descriptions]

3. **Implement to Pass Tests**
   - Implement minimum code to pass each test
   - Run tests after each change

4. **Refactor**
   - Clean up while keeping tests green
```

**TDD Workflow:**
```
Write test → Run (FAIL) → Implement → Run (PASS) → Refactor → Run (PASS)
```

### 5. Confidence Check

Run Pre-Implementation Confidence Check before proceeding.

### 6. Await Approval

Present plan and wait for user approval before implementation.

**Key review points for user:**
- Are the file changes correct?
- Is the approach sound?
- Any concerns about the changes?

## Example (Standard)

```
## Feature: Add rate limiting to API

### Requirements
- [ ] Limit requests to 100/minute per user
- [ ] Return 429 when exceeded
- [ ] Log rate limit hits

### Technical Approach
1. Add rate limiting middleware using existing Express pattern
   - Why: Consistent with authMiddleware.ts approach
2. Store counters in Redis (already used for sessions)

### Files to Modify

#### `src/middleware/rateLimitMiddleware.ts` (NEW)
**Purpose:** Rate limiting middleware
**Structure:**
- `rateLimiter()` - Express middleware
- `getRateKey()` - Generate Redis key

#### `src/app.ts` (line 23)
**Current:** Auth middleware only
**Change:** Add rate limiter after auth
```typescript
app.use(authMiddleware);
app.use(rateLimiter({ limit: 100, window: 60 })); // ADD
```

### Testing Strategy
- Unit tests: Mock Redis, test limit logic
- Integration tests: Hit endpoint 101 times
- Test file: `__tests__/middleware/rateLimitMiddleware.test.ts`

### Alternatives Considered
- express-rate-limit package - Adds dependency, we can do simpler

### Risks
- Redis connection issues - Fail open (allow requests)

### Complexity
- Medium - New middleware but follows existing patterns
```

```
/plan --tdd Add rate limiting to API
```

```

### TDD Implementation Order

1. **Acceptance Criteria → Test Cases**
   - [ ] Test: Returns 200 for requests under limit
   - [ ] Test: Returns 429 when limit exceeded

   - [ ] Test: Different users have separate limits

2. **Write Failing Tests First**

   describe('rateLimiter', () => {
     it('allows requests under limit', async () => { ... });
     it('returns 429 when limit exceeded', async () => { ... });
     it('resets after window expires', async () => { ... });
   });
   ```

3. **Implement to Pass Tests**
   - Create `rateLimitMiddleware.ts`
   - Implement `rateLimiter()` function
   - Run tests after each addition

Heading should never be negative. we use [0,360] for headings (or at least we should be). so a negative heading would be a valid sentinel

---

The GCS shouldn't auto-select ports anymore. And it needs to able to use UDP as well. See the changes that our other Claude session made:
● Yes — the SIL already uses two completely separate UDP sockets:

  1. CRRCSim socket — bound to port 9003, talks the sil-protocol binary format (IMU, GPS, actuators, etc.)
  2. MAVLink socket — bound to port 14550, talks MAVLink (heartbeat, attitude, params, etc.)

  They're independent file descriptors (sock_fd for crrcsim, _fd inside UdpTransport for MAVLink). Both use non-blocking
  receives. The background loop services MAVLink while the flight loop services crrcsim — same as the RP2350B where the
  flight loop reads sensors while the background loop handles USB telemetry.

  So yes, you can run crrcsim and QGroundControl (or smol_gcs) at the same time against the same SIL process. QGC listens
  on 14550 by default and should auto-discover.

Summary:
1. Primary Request and Intent:
   The user's primary request was to build Phase 3.5's GCS integration — a mission editor with Dubins path planning for the smol flight controller's ground control station (Elixir/Phoenix LiveView app at `tools/smol_gcs/`). This included:
   - A pure Elixir port of the C++ Dubins path planner for server-side path computation
   - A mission editor LiveView page with Leaflet map, waypoint placement, and Dubins path preview
   - MAVLink mission protocol messages for waypoint upload
   - Shared test vectors validating Elixir matches C++ reference
   - Removing serial auto-select and adding UDP transport support alongside USB serial
   - Debugging why the GCS receives only heartbeats (no telemetry) from the SIL over UDP

2. Key Technical Concepts:
   - Pure Elixir port of C++ header-only Dubins library (no NIF/Port, no JS)
   - Server-side path computation: LiveView computes paths, pushes pre-rendered lat/lon polylines to JS hook
   - FNV-1a path digest for cross-platform verification (C++ ↔ Elixir)
   - Float32 vs Float64 precision differences affecting path computation (coincident circle centers)
   - AGL altitude convention: MAV_FRAME_GLOBAL_RELATIVE_ALT_INT (frame=6), user enters AGL
   - Negative heading (-1.0) as sentinel for "auto-infer" instead of NaN (headings are [0,360])
   - Transport abstraction: Link GenServer dispatches send() to Serial or Udp
   - LinkEvents macro eliminates connection-handling boilerplate across 5 LiveViews
   - UDP peer discovery: FC learns GCS address from first received packet
   - MAVLink telemetry gating: ShouldSendMessage checks severity, interval, and has_data

   **Created - Transport Layer:**
   - `tools/smol_gcs/lib/smol_gcs/link.ex` — GenServer tracking active transport (:none/:usb/:udp), dispatches send() to Serial or Udp, handles connect_usb/connect_udp/disconnect
   - `tools/smol_gcs/lib/smol_gcs/udp.ex` — GenServer using :gen_udp with active:true, connect(host, port) opens ephemeral socket, parses inbound MAVLink via Parser, broadcasts to "mavlink:rx"
   - `tools/smol_gcs/lib/smol_gcs_web/live/link_events.ex` — `__using__` macro injecting handle_event clauses for open_link_picker, close_link_picker, connect_usb, connect_udp, disconnect_link. Also `link_assigns()` and `parse_udp_target/1`.

   **Created - Mission Upload:**
   - `tools/smol_gcs/lib/smol_gcs/mission.ex` — GenServer implementing MAVLink mission upload state machine (MISSION_COUNT → MISSION_REQUEST_INT → MISSION_ITEM_INT → MISSION_ACK). Uses Link.send, encode_heading (-1.0 for nil), encode_loiter_dir.

   **Created - Debugging:**
   - `docs/debugging/gcs-udp-telemetry-missing.md` — Documents the ongoing issue of GCS only receiving heartbeats over UDP

   **Created - Test Vectors:**
   - `lib/dubins/test_vectors.json` — 8 path + 4 mission test vectors with C++ reference digests

   **Modified - C++ Dubins Library:**
   - `lib/dubins/dubins/planner.h`:
     - Fixed CCC altitude distribution: added `mid_horiz` to `total_horiz` computation
     - Changed heading sentinel from NAN to -1.0f in PlanMission and InferHeading
   - `lib/dubins/dubins/types.h` — unchanged (reference)

   **Modified - C++ SIL:**
   - `src/hal/native/udp_transport.cpp` — Changed peer discovery from once-only to update-on-change:
     ```cpp
     bool addr_changed = _peer_known &&
                         (from_addr.sin_addr.s_addr != _peer_addr.sin_addr.s_addr ||
                          from_addr.sin_port != _peer_addr.sin_port);
     if (!_peer_known || addr_changed) {
         // update peer and print discovery/switch message
     }
     ```

   **Modified - GCS:**
   - `tools/smol_gcs/lib/smol_gcs/serial.ex` — Removed auto-port-selection from init
   - `tools/smol_gcs/lib/smol_gcs/application.ex` — Added Udp, Link to supervisor; renamed serial_children to transport_children
   - `tools/smol_gcs/lib/smol_gcs/heartbeat.ex` — SmolGcs.Serial.send → SmolGcs.Link.send
   - `tools/smol_gcs/lib/smol_gcs/telemetry.ex` — SmolGcs.Serial.send → SmolGcs.Link.send
   - `tools/smol_gcs/lib/smol_gcs_web/components/instruments.ex` — Added "Mission" to @nav_pages, changed nav_bar attr from serial_port to link_detail, replaced port_picker_modal with link_picker_modal (USB + UDP sections)
   - `tools/smol_gcs/lib/smol_gcs_web/router.ex` — Added `live "/mission", MissionLive`
   - `tools/smol_gcs/assets/js/app.js` — Added MissionMapHook import and registration
   - All 5 LiveViews (flight, params, logs, inspector, mission) — Added `use SmolGcsWeb.LinkEvents`, replaced Serial references with Link, updated templates for link_picker_modal
   - `tools/smol_gcs/test/mavlink/types_test.exs` — Added 5 new CRC extras (42,44,47,51,73), updated count from 22 to 27
   - `tools/smol_gcs/lib/smol_gcs/mavlink/message.ex` — No lasting changes (NaN encode_value was added then removed)

   **Modified - C++ Tests:**
   - `test/test_dubins_planner/test_dubins_planner.cpp` — MakeWaypoint uses -1.0f instead of NAN; single-waypoint test checks -1.0f return

   **Externally Modified (by user/other session):**
   - `src/param/param_store.h` — Added TelemVfrHud parameter
   - `tools/smol_gcs/assets/js/hooks/mission_map_hook.js` — Minor formatting changes

4. Errors and fixes:
   - **dubins_type_dirs mapping inverted**: RSR→{:cw,:cw} should be {:ccw,:ccw}. All 6 mappings were backwards. Fixed by swapping all entries in types.ex.
   - **Float32/64 coincident circle centers**: U-turn case produces degenerate geometry in float64 but works in float32 due to cos(π/2) ≈ -4.37e-8 in float32 vs 6.12e-17 in float64. Fixed by replacing degenerate test vector with 150° sharp turn, and adding midpoint theta selection for coincident centers in circle.ex.
   - **C++ CCC altitude distribution bug**: BuildSegments didn't include CCC mid arc in total_horiz, causing altitude overshoot for RLR/LRL paths (+44m for a 400m climb). Fixed by computing mid_horiz before total_horiz and including it. This was found through cross-platform porting.
   - **FC UDP peer locking**: UdpTransport only set _peer_known once, preventing GCS reconnection. Fixed to compare addresses and update on change.
   - **Elixir compilation warnings**: Unused variables in planner.ex (start→_start, lambda_end, end_entry_angle), struct update warnings (added %PathCandidate{} pattern match). Fixed all.
   - **Hidden input name="id" warning**: Phoenix warned about overriding form element ID. Changed to name="wp_id".
   - **User correction on JS port**: User expected Elixir, not JavaScript. Rewrote entire plan.
   - **User correction on altitude**: Changed from MSL to AGL convention with MAV_FRAME_GLOBAL_RELATIVE_ALT_INT.
   - **User correction on NaN heading**: Changed sentinel from NaN to -1.0 (negative heading) since headings are [0,360].
   - **User correction on 500 cycles**: I incorrectly assumed the SIL flight loop exits after 500 cycles. The SIL has its own main (`main_native_sil.cpp`) with `while (!sigint_received)`.

5. Problem Solving:
   **Solved:**
   - Complete Elixir Dubins planner with cross-platform digest validation (92 GCS tests, 112 C++ tests)
   - Mission editor LiveView with Leaflet map integration
   - MAVLink mission protocol messages (5 definitions)
   - Mission upload GenServer
   - Transport abstraction (Link + Udp + LinkEvents)
   - FC UDP peer locking bug

   **Ongoing - GCS UDP Telemetry Missing:**
   The SIL sends only heartbeats over UDP despite the flight loop running, CRRCSim connected, and airplane flyable. The telemetry pipeline (ProcessSnapshot → Send* → UdpTransport::Write) should send ATTITUDE, HIGHRES_IMU, etc. but raw packet capture shows only msg_id=0. Documented in `docs/debugging/gcs-udp-telemetry-missing.md`. Not yet determined whether ProcessSnapshot is being called, or if ShouldSendMessage is blocking all channels, or if Write() fails silently.

---

Is there a way to make crrcsim perform more like the flightloop::Run in smol? We use the hal::sleepuntilnextcycle function.:
void SleepUntilNextCycle() {
  if (replay_mode) {
    std::this_thread::yield();
    return;
  }
  next_cycle += kCyclePeriod;
  std::this_thread::sleep_until(next_cycle);
}

Yes, clean up the debug instrumentation

---

# Slop Command

Check the diff against main and remove all AI-generated slop introduced in this branch.

## What is "Slop"?

AI-generated code often has tells that make it look unnatural:

### 1. Over-Commenting
```typescript
// BAD: AI slop
// Get the user from the database
const user = await db.getUser(id); // Fetch user by ID

// GOOD: Self-documenting, no comment needed
const user = await db.getUser(id);
```

### 2. Defensive Overkill
```typescript
// BAD: Unnecessary defensive checks
function processUser(user: User) {
  if (!user) {
    throw new Error('User is required');
  }
  if (!user.id) {
    throw new Error('User must have an id');
  }
  // ... when caller already validates
}

// GOOD: Trust internal callers
function processUser(user: User) {
  // Just do the work - caller handles validation
}
```

### 3. Type Escapes
```typescript
// BAD: Casting to escape type issues
const data = response as any;
const items = (result as unknown as Item[]);

// GOOD: Fix the actual type
const data: ResponseType = response;
```

### 4. Inconsistent Style
- Different naming conventions than the file uses
- Different error handling patterns
- Different import styles
- Added JSDoc when file doesn't use it (or vice versa)

### 5. Unnecessary Try/Catch
```typescript
// BAD: Wrapping things that don't throw
try {
  const x = a + b;
  return x;
} catch (error) {
  console.error('Failed to add numbers', error);
  throw error;
}

// GOOD: Just do it
return a + b;
```

### 6. Verbose Logging
```typescript
// BAD: Logging everything
console.log('Starting process...');
console.log('User ID:', userId);
console.log('Processing...');
console.log('Done!');

// GOOD: Log meaningful events only (or nothing for simple ops)
```

## Workflow

### 1. Get the Diff

```bash
git diff main...HEAD
```

Identify all files changed in this branch.

### 2. For Each Changed File

1. Read the FULL file (not just the diff) to understand existing patterns
2. Compare new code against existing style:
   - Comment density
   - Error handling approach
   - Naming conventions
   - Type annotation style
   - Import organization

### 3. Identify Slop

Look for code that:
- Has MORE comments than surrounding code
- Has MORE defensive checks than similar code paths
- Uses `any` or type assertions
- Has different formatting/style than the file
- Adds try/catch around non-throwing code
- Adds logging that doesn't match file patterns

### 4. Fix It

Remove or adjust:
- Delete unnecessary comments
- Remove redundant validation (if callers are trusted)
- Fix types properly instead of casting
- Match existing code style
- Remove pointless try/catch
- Remove excessive logging

**Use Edit tool to make changes.**

### 5. Report

End with a **1-3 sentence summary only**:

```
Removed 4 unnecessary comments, 2 redundant null checks, and fixed
1 `any` cast in UserService.ts. Deleted try/catch wrapper in
processPayment() since the caller handles errors.
```

## What NOT to Remove

- Comments that explain non-obvious business logic
- Validation at system boundaries (user input, external APIs)
- Error handling that matches the file's existing patterns
- Logging that matches existing patterns
- Type assertions that are genuinely necessary

## Example

**Before (AI slop):**
```typescript
/**
 * Fetches user data from the database
 * @param userId - The ID of the user to fetch
 * @returns The user object or null if not found
 */
async function getUser(userId: string): Promise<User | null> {
  // Validate the user ID
  if (!userId) {
    throw new Error('userId is required');
  }

  try {
    // Fetch the user from database
    const user = await db.users.findOne({ id: userId });

    // Return the user
    return user as any as User;
  } catch (error) {
    // Log the error
    console.error('Failed to fetch user:', error);
    throw error;
  }
}
```

**After (cleaned):**
```typescript
async function getUser(userId: string): Promise<User | null> {
  return db.users.findOne({ id: userId });
}
```

**Report:** "Removed JSDoc (file doesn't use it), deleted redundant userId validation (TypeScript enforces it), removed try/catch (caller handles errors), fixed `any` cast by using proper return type."

## Notes

- Run AFTER implementation, before /review
- Focuses on style consistency, not functionality
- Be conservative - when unsure, leave it
- Check git diff after to verify changes make sense

Base directory for this skill: /home/ubuntu/.claude/skills/cp-review

# Code Review

Review all changes on the current branch against main.

## Process

### 1. Gather Changes

```bash
git diff main --name-only
```

If no changes, inform the user and stop.

For each changed file, read the FULL file (not just the diff) to understand context. Also run:

```bash
git diff main
```

### 2. Review Against Guidelines

#### Code Reads Like Prose
- Descriptive function and variable names — no abbreviations that require mental decoding
- Linear data flows — can you read top-to-bottom without jumping around?
- Efficient line count — no bloat, no unnecessary abstractions
- DRY — is anything duplicated that shouldn't be?
- Single responsibility — each function does ONE thing, each class has ONE purpose
- Testable — could you write a test for this without mocking half the system?

#### Make Invalid States Unrepresentable
- Constraints encoded in types, not runtime checks
- No scattered validation for the same invariant
- `std::optional`, enums, and constructors used to enforce validity

#### Trace the Data
- Where does each value come from? What constraints does it carry?
- Are there redundant conversions or unnecessary intermediates?
- Does every downstream consumer get what it expects?

#### Always Make It Better
- Did we touch code without improving it?
- Are there obvious improvements just outside the diff boundary? (note in suggestions, don't block)

#### Project Conventions (from CLAUDE.md)
- No docstrings unless asked
- No fallbacks — code works or fails loudly
- No dead code, no commented-out experiments
- No default arguments
- Leading underscores for class data members
- PascalCase functions, snake_case locals, kCamelCase constants
- "latest" not "last" for most recent values
- Parameter passing: pointer for mutation, const ref for read-only, const value for scalars

### 3. Check For Slop
- Comments that explain "what" instead of "why"
- Defensive checks for conditions that can't happen
- Unnecessary try/catch or error handling beyond system boundaries
- Verbose logging that doesn't match existing patterns
- Style inconsistencies with surrounding code

### 4. Present Results

```
## Review Summary

**Assessment**: [APPROVE / REQUEST CHANGES]

### Positive Findings
- What was done well

### Required Changes
- Issues that must be fixed (file:line references)

### Suggestions
- Optional improvements

### Convention Violations
- Any CLAUDE.md or guideline violations
```

Be specific with file:line references. Prioritize correctness and readability over micro-optimizations. If approved, suggest running `/validate-smol` next.

---

Base directory for this skill: /home/ubuntu/Documents/Github/smol/.claude/skills/validate-smol

# Validate smol

Run all automated checks for the smol flight controller. Activate `~/.venvs/smol` before every command.

## Checks

Run these in order. If a check fails, stop and report — do not continue to later checks.

### 1. Regenerate and format

Regenerate all generated files and run the formatter. This ensures we never commit stale generated code or unformatted source.

```bash
python3 protocol/generate.py
just format
```

Then verify the checks pass:

```bash
just check-format
just check-codegen
```

Both must pass. Generated files (`src/protocol/`) are excluded from formatting — the generator owns their style.

### 2. Native unit tests

```bash
just test-native
```

Report pass/fail count from the summary line (e.g., "118 test cases: 118 succeeded").

Known flaky: `test_smol_matches_full_after_full_sequence` (BUG-006, FullEkf nondeterminism). If ONLY this test fails, re-run once. If it fails twice, report it.

### 3. Thread sanitizer

```bash
just test-tsan
```

Catches data races in SharedState, ring buffer, and cross-thread communication. Requires `setarch -R` for ASLR compatibility on Linux 6.x.

### 4. Elixir GCS tests

```bash
just test-gcs
```

### 5. Native build

```bash
just build-native
```

### 6. RP2350B build (CMake)

```bash
just build-fc3
```

This catches missing source files in `CMakeLists.txt` and RP2350B-specific compilation errors that native builds miss.

### 7. Replay validation

```bash
just test-replay
```

This builds `native_full_ekf`, replays reference flight data through both EKFs, and checks RMS error bounds vs truth. Requires steps 4-5 to have passed.

## Report

```
## Validation Report

### Regenerate + format
[PASS — tree clean / PASS — N files updated / FAIL — details]

### Native tests
[PASS — N test cases: N succeeded / FAIL — details]

### Thread sanitizer
[PASS / FAIL — details]

### GCS tests
[PASS — N tests: N passed / FAIL — details]

### Native build
[PASS / FAIL]

### RP2350B build
[PASS / FAIL — details if failed]

### Replay validation
[PASS — N passed / FAIL — details]

### Summary
[READY TO SHIP / NEEDS FIXES — list what failed]
```

## Next Steps

- All pass: `/ship` to commit
- Failures: fix and re-run `/validate-smol`

This session is being continued from a previous conversation that ran out of context. The summary below covers the earlier portion of the conversation.

Summary:
1. Primary Request and Intent:
   The user's primary request was to continue debugging and improving the GCS mission editor with Dubins path planning. This session covered multiple sub-tasks:
   - Debug why the SIL sends only heartbeats over UDP (no telemetry)
   - Complete the LiveView migration from serial-only to Link abstraction (USB + UDP)
   - Fix SIL telemetry rate (was 75Hz, target 100Hz)
   - Fix CRRCSim timing to deliver physics at a stable 100Hz
   - Clean up all debug instrumentation
   - Run code review and validation
   - Add `kHeadingUnspecified` constant and fix heading wrapping to [0, 360)
   - Restructure path renderer to output labeled segments with colors
   - Debug Dubins path rendering issues (continuity, heading arrows, path type selection)

2. Key Technical Concepts:
   - MAVLink telemetry pipeline: BackgroundMain → ring buffer → ProcessSnapshot → ShouldSendMessage → Send → UdpTransport::Write
   - `CacheTelemConfigs()` must run after `params::Init()` — SIL had them in wrong order
   - Float32 precision loss when converting `sil_time_sec * 1e6f` to microseconds at large sim times — fixed with double promotion
   - CRRCSim FDM thread timing: `usleep(dt)` replaced with `std::this_thread::sleep_until(next_cycle)` for drift-free scheduling
   - Dubins path types (RSR, LSL, RSL, LSR, RLR, LRL) with internal direction convention: kCcw(-1) = center to LEFT = left turn physically
   - Heading sentinel: `kHeadingUnspecified = -1.0f`, planner checks `heading_deg < 0` (not float equality)
   - `atan2` returns [-180, 180] — must wrap to [0, 360) to avoid collision with negative heading sentinel
   - LinkEvents macro eliminates ~120 lines of duplicated port-picker handlers across 5 LiveViews
   - PathRenderer labeled segments: `%{role: "entry"|"straight"|"exit"|"mid", points: [...]}`

     ```cpp
     inline float WrapTo360(const float deg) {
       float r = fmodf(deg, 360.0f);
       return r < 0.0f ? r + 360.0f : r;
     }
     ```

   - **`lib/dubins/dubins/planner.h`**

     - Replaced `usleep(dt * 1e6)` with `std::this_thread::sleep_until(next_cycle)`:
     ```cpp
     using clock = std::chrono::steady_clock;
     const auto period = std::chrono::duration_cast<clock::duration>(
         std::chrono::duration<double>(Global::dt));
     auto next_cycle = clock::now();
     while (fdm_thread_running) {
         next_cycle += period;
         // ... physics update ...
         std::this_thread::sleep_until(next_cycle);
     }
     ```

4. Errors and fixes:
   - **GCS only received heartbeats over UDP**: Root cause was `heartbeat.ex` and `telemetry.ex` using `Serial.send` instead of `Link.send`. Fixed by changing both to `Link.send`.
   - **SIL telemetry interval=0**: `CacheTelemConfigs()` called before `params::Init()`. Fixed by moving to `LoadParams()`.
   - **75Hz instead of 100Hz telemetry**: Multiple factors:
     - Float32 precision in `Clock::Update` `sil_time_sec * 1e6f` — fixed with double promotion
     - CRRCSim fixed-sleep timing — fixed with `sleep_until(next_cycle)`
     - FDM lock contention with render thread limits to 80-88Hz — accepted as CRRCSim limitation
   - **User correction: "stop guessing, use debug statements"**: I was speculatively tracing code instead of adding printfs. User wanted empirical data.
   - **User correction: "109 seconds is fine for float32"**: I incorrectly blamed float32 precision at the `time_sec` level. The real issue was the `*1e6f` multiplication creating a value beyond float32's integer precision range.
   - **User correction: "You're wasting my time" on test reruns**: I re-ran tests to see failures instead of capturing output first time. Fixed validate-smol SKILL.md.
   - **User correction on float equality**: I used `== kHeadingUnspecified` for heading check. User said to use `< 0` since any negative heading is invalid.
   - **User correction on constant naming**: `kHeadingAuto` too ambiguous (sounds like bool), `kAutoInferHeading` also bool-like. Settled on `kHeadingUnspecified`.
   - **MissionLive crash on `center_north_m`**: Debug print referenced non-existent struct field. Fixed to use `seg.center` tuple.
   - **MissionLive crash on `length_m`**: Debug print referenced non-existent field. Fixed to compute from start_point/end_point.
   - **MissionLive crash on `rendered.transit`**: `render_leg` returns `%{path: ...}` not `%{transit: ...}`. Later changed to `%{segments: ...}`.
   - **Heading wrapping bug**: `infer_heading` returned `atan2` result [-180, 180]. Westward heading -89.7° collided with `heading < 0` sentinel. Fixed with `WrapTo360`/`wrap_to_360` in both C++ and Elixir.
   - **Router missing /mission**: Added `live "/mission", MissionLive` to router.ex.
   - **MissionMapHook not registered**: Added import and registration in app.js.
   - **Dubins test failures (4)**: `MakeWaypoint` used NAN but planner changed to `-1.0f` sentinel. Fixed to use `kHeadingUnspecified`. Single-waypoint test changed from `isnan(chi)` to `chi < 0.0f`.

5. Problem Solving:
   **Solved:**
   - GCS UDP telemetry: Serial.send → Link.send + CacheTelemConfigs ordering
   - SIL clock precision: double promotion for microsecond conversion
   - CRRCSim timing: sleep_until instead of usleep
   - Heading wrapping: [0, 360) instead of [-180, 180]

8. Current Work:
   The most recent work was debugging three issues with the mission editor's Dubins path rendering:
   1. **Heading arrows not visible** — JS hook sends `resolved_heading_deg` but arrows don't appear. Not yet investigated in browser devtools.
   2. **Path geometry not continuous** — Arc segments don't connect tangentially to straight segments. The `build_segments` function in `planner.ex` computes `line_start` from `point_on_arc(center_start, r_min, exit_angle, z)`, but the renderer interpolates arcs using `center + r*cos(start_angle + lambda*span*fraction)`. If lambda or angle conventions don't match, the endpoints won't align.
   3. **RSL chosen instead of LSL for CCW square** — Confirmed both C++ and Elixir agree. This is the shortest Dubins path mathematically, even though it's not intuitive.

   A debugging document was created at `docs/debugging/gcs-mission-editor.md` documenting all three issues.

   The user's last substantive request before the summary was: "Create a debugging document in @docs/debugging/ with the issues we have so far." which was completed.

   Debug logging is still present in `mission_live.ex` for ongoing investigation.

9. Optional Next Step:
   Continue debugging the three mission editor issues documented in `docs/debugging/gcs-mission-editor.md`. The most impactful next step is fixing the **path geometric discontinuity** (issue #2), as this is the core rendering bug. The approach from the debugging doc: "Add temporary log in `build_straight()` printing `line_start` and compare with the arc renderer's final point for the same `exit_angle`. If they don't match, the lambda direction is wrong in one of the two computations." Also check heading arrows in browser devtools to determine why they're not rendering.

# Backlog Mode

You are in **Backlog Mode** - documenting bugs and improvements WITHOUT implementing them.

**Reference skills based on issue domain:**
- API issues: Read `.claude/skills/api-design-patterns/SKILL.md`
- Frontend components: Read `.claude/skills/react-patterns/SKILL.md`
- Error handling: Read `.claude/skills/error-handler/SKILL.md`
- UX improvements: Read `.claude/skills/frontend-design/SKILL.md`

## Available Tools & When to Use Them

### Codebase Exploration
Use **Task tool with Explore subagent** for:
- Finding root causes of bugs
- Understanding current implementation
- Locating affected files and components
```
Task(subagent_type="Explore", prompt="Very thorough: find all code related to [X]")
```

### External Research
Use **Exa search** (`mcp__exa__exa_search`) for:
- Checking if others encountered the same bug
- Finding known fixes or workarounds
- Researching UI/UX best practices for similar features
```
mcp__exa__exa_search(query="[framework] [issue description] fix")
```

Use **Ref documentation** (`mcp__Ref__*`) for:
- Checking official framework/library docs
- Verifying correct API usage
- Finding recommended patterns
```
mcp__Ref__ref_search_documentation(query="[library] [feature] documentation")
```

### UI/UX Verification
Use **Playwright** (`mcp__playwright__*`) for UX issues:
- Navigate to the affected page
- Take screenshot of current state (for BACKLOG entry)
- Verify the issue exists as user described
- Document "before" state
```
mcp__playwright__browser_navigate(url="http://localhost:3000/path")
mcp__playwright__browser_take_screenshot(filename="backlog-ux-xxx-before.png")
```

### Complex Analysis
Use **Sequential thinking** (`mcp__sequential-thinking__sequentialthinking`) for:
- Multi-step root cause analysis
- Weighing multiple potential causes
- Structuring complex investigations

---

## Parallel Execution Strategy

You CAN run multiple subagents AND tools in parallel by making multiple tool calls in a single message. Use this for efficiency when tasks are **independent**.

### Multiple Subagents in Parallel

**When to use:**
- Bug/feature spans frontend + backend (separate concerns)
- Investigation touches multiple packages
- Need both code exploration AND documentation research
- Complex issue benefits from divide-and-conquer

**Example - Bug spanning layers:**
```
[Single message, multiple Task calls - all run simultaneously:]

Task(subagent_type="Explore", prompt="Very thorough: find tRPC handlers for [feature]")
Task(subagent_type="Explore", prompt="Very thorough: find React components rendering [feature]")
Task(subagent_type="documentation-researcher", prompt="Research [framework] best practices for [pattern]")
```

**Example - Multi-package investigation:**
```
Task(subagent_type="Explore", prompt="Search packages/trpc for [issue]")
Task(subagent_type="Explore", prompt="Search packages/features for [issue]")
Task(subagent_type="Explore", prompt="Search apps/web for [issue]")
```

### Subagents + Tools in Parallel

**Example - UX issue (all at once):**
```
Task(subagent_type="Explore", prompt="Find component code for [element]")
mcp__playwright__browser_navigate(url="http://localhost:3000/path")
mcp__exa__exa_search(query="UX best practices [pattern]")
```

### When to Stay Sequential

- Results from first search inform what to search next
- Need to confirm issue exists before deep diving
- Small codebase where one Explore is sufficient
- Risk of overlapping/duplicated search areas

**Example - Sequential dependency:**
```
1. First: Explore → discovers it's a Prisma schema issue
2. Then: Ref search → "Prisma relations documentation"
   (wouldn't know to search Prisma without step 1)
```

### Rule of Thumb
| Situation | Approach |
|-----------|----------|
| Know what to search for | **Parallel** - maximize speed |
| Need to discover what to search | **Sequential** - learn first |
| Large codebase, clear separation | **Parallel subagents** - divide and conquer |
| Small codebase or focused issue | **Single subagent** - avoid overhead |

## Workflow Loop

For each item, execute these steps IN ORDER:

### Step 1: Receive
- Accept ONE item at a time
- If user provides multiple, say: "Let's start with the first one. What is it?"
- If `We have a lot of changs that I want to get merged into main. So let's make this a backlog item.
1. We need a way to validate paths. We are creating paths with discontinuities. these should be caught and flagged as impossible.
2. We need to fix the infer_heading logic.
3. There should ALWAYS be a viable dubins path as long as the points are far away enough, which they are for the racetrack and figure 8 case. Even if the headings were selected sub-optimally, a viable path still should have been created.` provided, use that as the item

### Step 2: Classify
Determine type based on description:
| Type | Criteria |
|------|----------|
| **BUG** | Something broken, error, unexpected behavior |
| **ENH** | New feature, capability, or functional improvement |
| **UX** | Visual, usability, or interface improvement |

State your classification: "This sounds like a **[TYPE]**."

### Step 3: Check Duplicates
- Read BACKLOG.md
- Search for similar existing entries
- If potential duplicate found: "This might be related to [ID]. Is this the same issue or different?"

### Step 4: Investigate (Use Appropriate Tools)

**For ALL types:**
- Use **Explore subagent** to find relevant code

**For BUGs additionally:**
- Use **Exa** to search if others hit this issue
- Check for known fixes or workarounds

**For ENH additionally:**
- Use **Ref** to check official docs for best practices
- Use **Exa** to research how others implement similar features

**For UX additionally:**
- Use **Playwright** to navigate to the page and take a screenshot
- Verify the issue exists as described
- Save screenshot as `backlog-ux-XXX-current.png` for documentation

### Step 5: Analyze
Use sequential thinking if complex. Summarize:
- What you found in codebase
- What external research revealed (if any)
- Root cause (BUG) or approach (ENH/UX)
- All affected files with full paths
- Suggested priority (P1/P2/P3)

### Step 6: Preview Entry
Show the complete BACKLOG entry to user:
```
Here's the proposed entry:

### [TYPE-XXX] Title
- **Reported**: date
- **Status**: Open
...

Does this look accurate? Any changes?
```

### Step 7: Document
After user confirms (or says "looks good", "yes", "ok"):
- Add entry to appropriate section in BACKLOG.md
- Update Statistics section
- Confirm: "Added as **[TYPE-XXX]** to BACKLOG.md"

### Step 8: Next Item
Ask: "Next item? (or 'done' to exit backlog mode)"
- If user provides another item → Go to Step 1
- If user says "done", "exit", "that's all" → End with summary of items added

---

## Critical Rules

1. **NO IMPLEMENTATION** - Only analyze and document
2. **NO CODE CHANGES** - Only read/explore, write only to BACKLOG.md
3. **ALWAYS PREVIEW** - Never add without user confirmation
4. **ONE AT A TIME** - Don't batch multiple items
5. **USE SUBAGENTS** - For thorough codebase exploration
6. **RESEARCH WHEN RELEVANT** - Use Exa/Ref for external context
7. **SCREENSHOT UX ISSUES** - Visual documentation helps
8. **INCREMENT IDs** - Check highest existing ID, add 1

---

## Priority Guidelines

| Priority | Use When |
|----------|----------|
| **P1 (Critical)** | Blocks core functionality, security risk, data loss, affects all users |
| **P2 (Medium)** | Significant but has workaround, important feature request |
| **P3 (Low)** | Minor issue, cosmetic, nice-to-have |

# Slop Command

Check the diff against main and remove all AI-generated slop introduced in this branch.

## What is "Slop"?

AI-generated code often has tells that make it look unnatural:

### 1. Over-Commenting
```typescript
// BAD: AI slop
// Get the user from the database
const user = await db.getUser(id); // Fetch user by ID

// GOOD: Self-documenting, no comment needed
const user = await db.getUser(id);
```

### 2. Defensive Overkill
```typescript
// BAD: Unnecessary defensive checks
function processUser(user: User) {
  if (!user) {
    throw new Error('User is required');
  }
  if (!user.id) {
    throw new Error('User must have an id');
  }
  // ... when caller already validates
}

// GOOD: Trust internal callers
function processUser(user: User) {
  // Just do the work - caller handles validation
}
```

### 3. Type Escapes
```typescript
// BAD: Casting to escape type issues
const data = response as any;
const items = (result as unknown as Item[]);

// GOOD: Fix the actual type
const data: ResponseType = response;
```

### 4. Inconsistent Style
- Different naming conventions than the file uses
- Different error handling patterns
- Different import styles
- Added JSDoc when file doesn't use it (or vice versa)

### 5. Unnecessary Try/Catch
```typescript
// BAD: Wrapping things that don't throw
try {
  const x = a + b;
  return x;
} catch (error) {
  console.error('Failed to add numbers', error);
  throw error;
}

// GOOD: Just do it
return a + b;
```

### 6. Verbose Logging
```typescript
// BAD: Logging everything
console.log('Starting process...');
console.log('User ID:', userId);
console.log('Processing...');
console.log('Done!');

// GOOD: Log meaningful events only (or nothing for simple ops)
```

## Workflow

### 1. Get the Diff

```bash
git diff main...HEAD
```

Identify all files changed in this branch.

### 2. For Each Changed File

1. Read the FULL file (not just the diff) to understand existing patterns
2. Compare new code against existing style:
   - Comment density
   - Error handling approach
   - Naming conventions
   - Type annotation style
   - Import organization

### 3. Identify Slop

Look for code that:
- Has MORE comments than surrounding code
- Has MORE defensive checks than similar code paths
- Uses `any` or type assertions
- Has different formatting/style than the file
- Adds try/catch around non-throwing code
- Adds logging that doesn't match file patterns

### 4. Fix It

Remove or adjust:
- Delete unnecessary comments
- Remove redundant validation (if callers are trusted)
- Fix types properly instead of casting
- Match existing code style
- Remove pointless try/catch
- Remove excessive logging

**Use Edit tool to make changes.**

### 5. Report

End with a **1-3 sentence summary only**:

```
Removed 4 unnecessary comments, 2 redundant null checks, and fixed
1 `any` cast in UserService.ts. Deleted try/catch wrapper in
processPayment() since the caller handles errors.
```

## What NOT to Remove

- Comments that explain non-obvious business logic
- Validation at system boundaries (user input, external APIs)
- Error handling that matches the file's existing patterns
- Logging that matches existing patterns
- Type assertions that are genuinely necessary

## Example

**Before (AI slop):**
```typescript
/**
 * Fetches user data from the database
 * @param userId - The ID of the user to fetch
 * @returns The user object or null if not found
 */
async function getUser(userId: string): Promise<User | null> {
  // Validate the user ID
  if (!userId) {
    throw new Error('userId is required');
  }

  try {
    // Fetch the user from database
    const user = await db.users.findOne({ id: userId });

    // Return the user
    return user as any as User;
  } catch (error) {
    // Log the error
    console.error('Failed to fetch user:', error);
    throw error;
  }
}
```

**After (cleaned):**
```typescript
async function getUser(userId: string): Promise<User | null> {
  return db.users.findOne({ id: userId });
}
```

**Report:** "Removed JSDoc (file doesn't use it), deleted redundant userId validation (TypeScript enforces it), removed try/catch (caller handles errors), fixed `any` cast by using proper return type."

## Notes

- Run AFTER implementation, before /review
- Focuses on style consistency, not functionality
- Be conservative - when unsure, leave it
- Check git diff after to verify changes make sense

# Code Review

Review all changes on the current branch against main.

## Process

### 1. Gather Changes

```bash
git diff main --name-only
```

If no changes, inform the user and stop.

For each changed file, read the FULL file (not just the diff) to understand context. Also run:

```bash
git diff main
```

### 2. Review Against Guidelines

#### Code Reads Like Prose
- Descriptive function and variable names — no abbreviations that require mental decoding
- Linear data flows — can you read top-to-bottom without jumping around?
- Efficient line count — no bloat, no unnecessary abstractions
- DRY — is anything duplicated that shouldn't be?
- Single responsibility — each function does ONE thing, each class has ONE purpose
- Testable — could you write a test for this without mocking half the system?

#### Make Invalid States Unrepresentable
- Constraints encoded in types, not runtime checks
- No scattered validation for the same invariant
- `std::optional`, enums, and constructors used to enforce validity

#### Trace the Data
- Where does each value come from? What constraints does it carry?
- Are there redundant conversions or unnecessary intermediates?
- Does every downstream consumer get what it expects?

#### Always Make It Better
- Did we touch code without improving it?
- Are there obvious improvements just outside the diff boundary? (note in suggestions, don't block)

#### Project Conventions (from CLAUDE.md)
- No docstrings unless asked
- No fallbacks — code works or fails loudly
- No dead code, no commented-out experiments
- No default arguments
- Leading underscores for class data members
- PascalCase functions, snake_case locals, kCamelCase constants
- "latest" not "last" for most recent values
- Parameter passing: pointer for mutation, const ref for read-only, const value for scalars

### 3. Check For Slop
- Comments that explain "what" instead of "why"
- Defensive checks for conditions that can't happen
- Unnecessary try/catch or error handling beyond system boundaries
- Verbose logging that doesn't match existing patterns
- Style inconsistencies with surrounding code

### 4. Present Results

```
## Review Summary

**Assessment**: [APPROVE / REQUEST CHANGES]

### Positive Findings
- What was done well

### Required Changes
- Issues that must be fixed (file:line references)

### Suggestions
- Optional improvements

### Convention Violations
- Any CLAUDE.md or guideline violations
```

Be specific with file:line references. Prioritize correctness and readability over micro-optimizations. If approved, suggest running `/validate-smol` next.

3. fix test_vectors.json so the tests pass
