# Validate smol

Run all automated checks for the smol flight controller. Activate `~/.venvs/smol` before every command.

**CRITICAL**: Capture the FULL output of every command. Never re-run a command just to see which tests failed — read the output you already have. Use `2>&1` to merge stderr, and save long outputs to a file if needed.

## Checks

Run these in order. If a check fails, stop and report — do not continue to later checks.

### 1. Regenerate and format

Regenerate all generated files and run the formatter. This ensures we never commit stale generated code or unformatted source.

```bash
python3 protocol/generate.py && just format && just check-format && just check-codegen
```

Both checks must pass. Generated files (`src/protocol/`) are excluded from formatting — the generator owns their style.

### 2. Native unit tests

```bash
just test-native 2>&1 | tee /tmp/smol-test-native.txt
```

Read the FULL output to find failures. Do NOT re-run just to see which tests failed.

Report pass/fail count from the summary line (e.g., "118 test cases: 118 succeeded").

Known flaky: `test_smol_matches_full_after_full_sequence` (BUG-006, FullEkf nondeterminism). If ONLY this test fails, re-run once. If it fails twice, report it.

### 3. Thread sanitizer

```bash
just test-tsan 2>&1 | tee /tmp/smol-test-tsan.txt
```

Catches data races in SharedState, ring buffer, and cross-thread communication. Requires `setarch -R` for ASLR compatibility on Linux 6.x.

### 4. Elixir GCS tests

```bash
just test-gcs 2>&1 | tee /tmp/smol-test-gcs.txt
```

### 5. Native build

```bash
just build-native
```

### 6. RP2350B build (CMake)

```bash
just build-fc3
```

This catches missing source files in `CMakeLists.txt` and RP2350B-specific compilation errors that native builds miss.

### 7. Replay validation

```bash
just test-replay 2>&1 | tee /tmp/smol-test-replay.txt
```

This builds `native_full_ekf`, replays reference flight data through both EKFs, and checks RMS error bounds vs truth. Requires steps 4-5 to have passed.

## Report

```
## Validation Report

### Regenerate + format
[PASS — tree clean / PASS — N files updated / FAIL — details]

### Native tests
[PASS — N test cases: N succeeded / FAIL — details]

### Thread sanitizer
[PASS / FAIL — details]

### GCS tests
[PASS — N tests: N passed / FAIL — details]

### Native build
[PASS / FAIL]

### RP2350B build
[PASS / FAIL — details if failed]

### Replay validation
[PASS — N passed / FAIL — details]

### Summary
[READY TO SHIP / NEEDS FIXES — list what failed]
```

## Next Steps

- All pass: `/ship` to commit
- Failures: fix and re-run `/validate-smol`

This session is being continued from a previous conversation that ran out of context. The summary below covers the earlier portion of the conversation.

Summary:
1. Primary Request and Intent:
   The user's primary goal was to debug and fix the GCS mission editor's Dubins path rendering. This evolved into several sub-tasks:
   - Test the C++ Dubins path planner with a racetrack pattern to verify correctness
   - Fix the discovered R↔L direction naming inversion in the DubinsType enum
   - Create hand-computed reference test vectors for cross-platform verification
   - Add test pattern buttons (racetrack, figure-8) to the mission editor for repeatable testing
   - Debug why auto-inferred headings produce invalid-looking paths
   - Document path planner bugs in the backlog (BUG-007)
   - Run slop check, code review, validation, then ship as PR #53
   - Address PR review comments (upload timeout, target IDs from heartbeat)

2. Key Technical Concepts:
   - Dubins path types (RSR, LSL, RSL, LSR, RLR, LRL) and their direction conventions
   - TurnDir enum: kCw (+1) = clockwise = right turn, kCcw (-1) = counterclockwise = left turn
   - The R↔L inversion bug: kRSR was mapping to kCcw (left turns) when it should map to kCw (right turns). Geometry was always correct, only the enum labels were inverted.
   - `infer_heading` uses bearing to NEXT waypoint, but intermediate waypoints need through-headings matching arrival direction. This causes 90° heading mismatches at corners, forcing cross-tangent paths with wild detours.
   - FNV-1a path digest for cross-platform verification (C++ ↔ Elixir)
   - PathCandidate struct defaults: fields should default to 0.0 in the struct rather than using `|| 0.0` fallbacks at every use site
   - MAVLink mission upload protocol: sequential MISSION_COUNT → N×REQUEST/ITEM round-trips → ACK
   - Vehicle state stores fc_sysid/fc_compid from heartbeat for mission targeting

3. Files and Code Sections:

   - **lib/dubins/dubins/planner.h**
     - Critical R↔L direction fix in Compute2DCandidate switch statement
     - Now: kRSR→kCw,kCw; kLSL→kCcw,kCcw; kRSL→kCw,kCcw; kLSR→kCcw,kCw; kRLR→kCw,kCw; kLRL→kCcw,kCcw
     - Added comment: "R = Right turn = kCw (clockwise, center east of north-heading vehicle)"
     - InferHeading now uses WrapTo360 and returns kHeadingUnspecified for count < 2

   - **lib/dubins/dubins/types.h**
     - Added `inline constexpr float kHeadingUnspecified = -1.0f;` before Waypoint struct
     - TurnDir comments: kCw (+1) = clockwise orbit, center east of north-heading vehicle; kCcw (-1) = counterclockwise

   - **lib/dubins/dubins/math_utils.h**
     - Added WrapTo360: wraps degrees to [0, 360)

   - **tools/smol_gcs/lib/smol_gcs/dubins/types.ex**
     - Fixed dubins_type_dirs to match C++:
       ```elixir
       def dubins_type_dirs(:rsr), do: {:cw, :cw}
       def dubins_type_dirs(:lsl), do: {:ccw, :ccw}
       def dubins_type_dirs(:rsl), do: {:cw, :ccw}
       def dubins_type_dirs(:lsr), do: {:ccw, :cw}
       def dubins_type_dirs(:rlr), do: {:cw, :cw}
       def dubins_type_dirs(:lrl), do: {:ccw, :ccw}

   - **tools/smol_gcs/lib/smol_gcs/dubins/planner.ex**

# Plan Command

Plan a new feature or task with proper structure before implementation.

**Reference skills based on feature type:**
- API/backend: Read `.claude/skills/api-design-patterns/SKILL.md`
- React components: Read `.claude/skills/react-patterns/SKILL.md`
- UI styling: Read `.claude/skills/tailwind-conventions/SKILL.md`
- Error handling: Read `.claude/skills/error-handler/SKILL.md`
- TDD mode: Read `.claude/skills/test-generator/SKILL.md`

**For new projects:** Use `/greenfield` first to define specs, then `/plan` for implementation.

## Flags

- `--tdd` - Enable Test-Driven Development mode (write tests first)

## Validation

If no feature description provided, ask for one.

## Planning Steps

### 1. Gather Context (REQUIRED)

**You MUST read relevant files before creating a plan.** Don't plan based on assumptions.

Before planning:
- Read relevant CLAUDE.md files
- **Read the actual files** that will be modified
- Identify existing patterns and conventions
- Understand related code and dependencies

Use `Explore` agent or direct file reads to understand:
- Current implementation
- Existing patterns in similar code
- Test file locations and patterns

### 2. Requirements Clarification

Ask clarifying questions if needed:
- What is the expected behavior?
- What are the edge cases?
- What are the acceptance criteria?
- Are there performance requirements?

### 3. Create Plan

Structure the implementation with **specific details**:

**Detail Level Guidelines:**

| Change Type | Detail Level |
|-------------|--------------|
| Complex/risky changes | Line numbers + code snippets |
| Medium changes | Function/method names |
| Simple/obvious changes | File paths only |
| New files | File path + structure outline |

**Output Format:**
```
## Feature: [description]

### Requirements
- [ ] Requirement 1
- [ ] Requirement 2

### Technical Approach
1. Step 1 - [description]
   - Why: [reasoning for this approach]
2. Step 2 - [description]

### Files to Modify

#### `path/to/file.ts` (lines 45-67)
**Current:** [brief description of current state]
**Change:** [what will change]
```typescript
// Example of the change (for complex modifications)
function existingFunction() {
  // Add: new caching logic here
}
```

#### `path/to/new-file.ts` (NEW)
**Purpose:** [why this file is needed]
**Structure:**
- `functionA()` - [purpose]
- `functionB()` - [purpose]

### Dependencies
- [list any new dependencies]

### Testing Strategy
- Unit tests: [specific test cases]
- Integration tests: [approach]
- Test file: `path/to/tests/file.test.ts`

### Alternatives Considered
- [Alternative 1] - [why not chosen]

### Risks
- [potential issue] - [mitigation]

### Complexity
- [low/medium/high] - [justification]
```

### 4. TDD Mode (if --tdd flag)

When `--tdd` is specified, modify the plan to include:

```
### TDD Implementation Order

1. **Acceptance Criteria → Test Cases**
   - [ ] Test: [criteria 1 as test]
   - [ ] Test: [criteria 2 as test]

2. **Write Failing Tests First**
   Files to create/modify:
   - `__tests__/feature.test.ts` - [test descriptions]

3. **Implement to Pass Tests**
   - Implement minimum code to pass each test
   - Run tests after each change

4. **Refactor**
   - Clean up while keeping tests green
```

**TDD Workflow:**
```
Write test → Run (FAIL) → Implement → Run (PASS) → Refactor → Run (PASS)
```

### 5. Confidence Check

Run Pre-Implementation Confidence Check before proceeding.

### 6. Await Approval

Present plan and wait for user approval before implementation.

**Key review points for user:**
- Are the file changes correct?
- Is the approach sound?
- Any concerns about the changes?

## Example (Standard)

```
## Feature: Add rate limiting to API

### Requirements
- [ ] Limit requests to 100/minute per user
- [ ] Return 429 when exceeded
- [ ] Log rate limit hits

### Technical Approach
1. Add rate limiting middleware using existing Express pattern
   - Why: Consistent with authMiddleware.ts approach
2. Store counters in Redis (already used for sessions)

### Files to Modify

#### `src/middleware/rateLimitMiddleware.ts` (NEW)
**Purpose:** Rate limiting middleware
**Structure:**
- `rateLimiter()` - Express middleware
- `getRateKey()` - Generate Redis key

#### `src/app.ts` (line 23)
**Current:** Auth middleware only
**Change:** Add rate limiter after auth
```typescript
app.use(authMiddleware);
app.use(rateLimiter({ limit: 100, window: 60 })); // ADD
```

### Testing Strategy
- Unit tests: Mock Redis, test limit logic
- Integration tests: Hit endpoint 101 times
- Test file: `__tests__/middleware/rateLimitMiddleware.test.ts`

### Alternatives Considered
- express-rate-limit package - Adds dependency, we can do simpler

### Risks
- Redis connection issues - Fail open (allow requests)

### Complexity
- Medium - New middleware but follows existing patterns
```

```
/plan --tdd Add rate limiting to API

```
## Feature: Add rate limiting to API (TDD)

### TDD Implementation Order

1. **Acceptance Criteria → Test Cases**
   - [ ] Test: Returns 200 for requests under limit
   - [ ] Test: Returns 429 when limit exceeded
   - [ ] Test: Resets after window expires
   - [ ] Test: Different users have separate limits

2. **Write Failing Tests First**
   File: `__tests__/middleware/rateLimitMiddleware.test.ts`
   ```typescript
   describe('rateLimiter', () => {
     it('allows requests under limit', async () => { ... });
     it('returns 429 when limit exceeded', async () => { ... });
     it('resets after window expires', async () => { ... });
   });
   ```

3. **Implement to Pass Tests**
   - Create `rateLimitMiddleware.ts`
   - Implement `rateLimiter()` function
   - Run tests after each addition

4. **Refactor**
   - Extract Redis key generation
   - Add JSDoc comments
```

After approval:
- If `--tdd`: Write tests first, then implement
- Otherwise: Start implementation
- Use `/review` for code review
- Use `/validate` to verify before completion
- Use `/ship` when ready to commit


ARGUMENTS: We need to work on BUG-007 in the backlog

---

This session is being continued from a previous conversation that ran out of context. The summary below covers the earlier portion of the conversation.

Summary:
1. Primary Request and Intent:
   The user's primary request was to build Phase 3.5's GCS integration — a mission editor with Dubins path planning for the smol flight controller's ground control station (Elixir/Phoenix LiveView app at `tools/smol_gcs/`). This included:
   - A pure Elixir port of the C++ Dubins path planner for server-side path computation
   - A mission editor LiveView page with Leaflet map, waypoint placement, and Dubins path preview
   - MAVLink mission protocol messages for waypoint upload
   - Shared test vectors validating Elixir matches C++ reference
   - Removing serial auto-select and adding UDP transport support alongside USB serial
   - Debugging why the GCS receives only heartbeats (no telemetry) from the SIL over UDP

2. Key Technical Concepts:
   - Pure Elixir port of C++ header-only Dubins library (no NIF/Port, no JS)
   - Server-side path computation: LiveView computes paths, pushes pre-rendered lat/lon polylines to JS hook
   - FNV-1a path digest for cross-platform verification (C++ ↔ Elixir)
   - Float32 vs Float64 precision differences affecting path computation (coincident circle centers)
   - AGL altitude convention: MAV_FRAME_GLOBAL_RELATIVE_ALT_INT (frame=6), user enters AGL
   - Negative heading (-1.0) as sentinel for "auto-infer" instead of NaN (headings are [0,360])
   - Transport abstraction: Link GenServer dispatches send() to Serial or Udp
   - LinkEvents macro eliminates connection-handling boilerplate across 5 LiveViews
   - UDP peer discovery: FC learns GCS address from first received packet
   - MAVLink telemetry gating: ShouldSendMessage checks severity, interval, and has_data

3. Files and Code Sections:

   **Created - Elixir Dubins Library:**
   - `tools/smol_gcs/lib/smol_gcs/dubins/types.ex` — Structs (Pose, Waypoint, PathSegment, DubinsPath, MissionLeg), turn_dir helpers, dubins_type_dirs mapping
   - `tools/smol_gcs/lib/smol_gcs/dubins/math.ex` — WrapTo2Pi, WrapToPi, angle_diff_rad, dist_2d, clampf, to_rad/to_deg
   - `tools/smol_gcs/lib/smol_gcs/dubins/circle.ex` — circle_center, angle_on_circle, arc_span (with 1e-4 guard), outer/cross tangents, CCC geometry. Coincident center fix: uses midpoint theta when dist < 1e-6
   - `tools/smol_gcs/lib/smol_gcs/dubins/planner.ex` — InternalPose, PathCandidate, compute_2d_candidate, compute_helix_turns, compute_gamma, build_segments, compute_dubins_path, infer_heading, plan_mission
   - `tools/smol_gcs/lib/smol_gcs/dubins/digest.ex` — FNV-1a hash (fnv_hash with little-endian byte extraction, quantize at 1mm/0.001rad)
   - `tools/smol_gcs/lib/smol_gcs/dubins/geo.ex` — lla_to_ned, ned_to_lla (flat-earth, @earth_radius_m = 6_371_000)

                          from_addr.sin_port != _peer_addr.sin_port);
     if (!_peer_known || addr_changed) {
         // update peer and print discovery/switch message
     }
     ```

4. Errors and fixes:
   - **dubins_type_dirs mapping inverted**: RSR→{:cw,:cw} should be {:ccw,:ccw}. All 6 mappings were backwards. Fixed by swapping all entries in types.ex.
   - **Float32/64 coincident circle centers**: U-turn case produces degenerate geometry in float64 but works in float32 due to cos(π/2) ≈ -4.37e-8 in float32 vs 6.12e-17 in float64. Fixed by replacing degenerate test vector with 150° sharp turn, and adding midpoint theta selection for coincident centers in circle.ex.
   - **C++ CCC altitude distribution bug**: BuildSegments didn't include CCC mid arc in total_horiz, causing altitude overshoot for RLR/LRL paths (+44m for a 400m climb). Fixed by computing mid_horiz before total_horiz and including it. This was found through cross-platform porting.
   - **FC UDP peer locking**: UdpTransport only set _peer_known once, preventing GCS reconnection. Fixed to compare addresses and update on change.
   - **Elixir compilation warnings**: Unused variables in planner.ex (start→_start, lambda_end, end_entry_angle), struct update warnings (added %PathCandidate{} pattern match). Fixed all.
   - **Hidden input name="id" warning**: Phoenix warned about overriding form element ID. Changed to name="wp_id".
   - **User correction on JS port**: User expected Elixir, not JavaScript. Rewrote entire plan.
   - **User correction on altitude**: Changed from MSL to AGL convention with MAV_FRAME_GLOBAL_RELATIVE_ALT_INT.
   - **User correction on NaN heading**: Changed sentinel from NaN to -1.0 (negative heading) since headings are [0,360].
   - **User correction on 500 cycles**: I incorrectly assumed the SIL flight loop exits after 500 cycles. The SIL has its own main (`main_native_sil.cpp`) with `while (!sigint_received)`.

5. Problem Solving:
   **Solved:**
   - Complete Elixir Dubins planner with cross-platform digest validation (92 GCS tests, 112 C++ tests)
   - Mission editor LiveView with Leaflet map integration
   - MAVLink mission protocol messages (5 definitions)
   - Mission upload GenServer
   - Transport abstraction (Link + Udp + LinkEvents)
   - FC UDP peer locking bug

   **Ongoing - GCS UDP Telemetry Missing:**
   The SIL sends only heartbeats over UDP despite the flight loop running, CRRCSim connected, and airplane flyable. The telemetry pipeline (ProcessSnapshot → Send* → UdpTransport::Write) should send ATTITUDE, HIGHRES_IMU, etc. but raw packet capture shows only msg_id=0. Documented in `docs/debugging/gcs-udp-telemetry-missing.md`. Not yet determined whether ProcessSnapshot is being called, or if ShouldSendMessage is blocking all channels, or if Write() fails silently.

Is there a way to make crrcsim perform more like the flightloop::Run in smol? We use the hal::sleepuntilnextcycle function.:
void SleepUntilNextCycle() {
  if (replay_mode) {
    std::this_thread::yield();
    return;
  }
  next_cycle += kCyclePeriod;
  std::this_thread::sleep_until(next_cycle);
}

Yes, clean up the debug instrumentation

---

# Slop Command

Check the diff against main and remove all AI-generated slop introduced in this branch.

## What is "Slop"?

AI-generated code often has tells that make it look unnatural:

### 1. Over-Commenting
```typescript
// BAD: AI slop
// Get the user from the database
const user = await db.getUser(id); // Fetch user by ID

// GOOD: Self-documenting, no comment needed
const user = await db.getUser(id);
```

### 2. Defensive Overkill
```typescript
// BAD: Unnecessary defensive checks
function processUser(user: User) {
  if (!user) {
    throw new Error('User is required');
  }
  if (!user.id) {
    throw new Error('User must have an id');
  }
  // ... when caller already validates
}

// GOOD: Trust internal callers
function processUser(user: User) {
  // Just do the work - caller handles validation
}
```

### 3. Type Escapes
```typescript
// BAD: Casting to escape type issues
const data = response as any;
const items = (result as unknown as Item[]);

// GOOD: Fix the actual type
const data: ResponseType = response;
```

### 4. Inconsistent Style
- Different naming conventions than the file uses
- Different error handling patterns
- Different import styles
- Added JSDoc when file doesn't use it (or vice versa)

### 5. Unnecessary Try/Catch
```typescript
// BAD: Wrapping things that don't throw
try {
  const x = a + b;
  return x;
} catch (error) {
  console.error('Failed to add numbers', error);
  throw error;
}

// GOOD: Just do it
return a + b;
```

### 6. Verbose Logging
```typescript
// BAD: Logging everything
console.log('Starting process...');
console.log('User ID:', userId);
console.log('Processing...');
console.log('Done!');

// GOOD: Log meaningful events only (or nothing for simple ops)
```

## Workflow

### 1. Get the Diff

```bash
git diff main...HEAD
```

Identify all files changed in this branch.

### 2. For Each Changed File

1. Read the FULL file (not just the diff) to understand existing patterns
2. Compare new code against existing style:
   - Comment density
   - Error handling approach
   - Naming conventions
   - Type annotation style
   - Import organization

### 3. Identify Slop

Look for code that:
- Has MORE comments than surrounding code
- Has MORE defensive checks than similar code paths
- Uses `any` or type assertions
- Has different formatting/style than the file
- Adds try/catch around non-throwing code
- Adds logging that doesn't match file patterns

### 4. Fix It

Remove or adjust:
- Delete unnecessary comments
- Remove redundant validation (if callers are trusted)
- Fix types properly instead of casting
- Match existing code style
- Remove pointless try/catch
- Remove excessive logging

**Use Edit tool to make changes.**

### 5. Report

End with a **1-3 sentence summary only**:

```
Removed 4 unnecessary comments, 2 redundant null checks, and fixed
1 `any` cast in UserService.ts. Deleted try/catch wrapper in
processPayment() since the caller handles errors.
```

## What NOT to Remove

- Comments that explain non-obvious business logic
- Validation at system boundaries (user input, external APIs)
- Error handling that matches the file's existing patterns
- Logging that matches existing patterns
- Type assertions that are genuinely necessary

## Example

**Before (AI slop):**
```typescript
/**
 * Fetches user data from the database
 * @param userId - The ID of the user to fetch
 * @returns The user object or null if not found
 */
async function getUser(userId: string): Promise<User | null> {
  // Validate the user ID
  if (!userId) {
    throw new Error('userId is required');
  }

  try {
    // Fetch the user from database
    const user = await db.users.findOne({ id: userId });

    // Return the user
    return user as any as User;
  } catch (error) {
    // Log the error
    console.error('Failed to fetch user:', error);
    throw error;
  }
}
```

**After (cleaned):**
```typescript
async function getUser(userId: string): Promise<User | null> {
  return db.users.findOne({ id: userId });
}
```

**Report:** "Removed JSDoc (file doesn't use it), deleted redundant userId validation (TypeScript enforces it), removed try/catch (caller handles errors), fixed `any` cast by using proper return type."

## Notes

- Run AFTER implementation, before /review
- Focuses on style consistency, not functionality
- Be conservative - when unsure, leave it
- Check git diff after to verify changes make sense


ARGUMENTS: look at all files that are different compared to main

Base directory for this skill: /home/ubuntu/.claude/skills/cp-review

# Code Review

Review all changes on the current branch against main.

## Process

### 1. Gather Changes

```bash
git diff main --name-only
```

If no changes, inform the user and stop.

For each changed file, read the FULL file (not just the diff) to understand context. Also run:

```bash
git diff main
```

### 2. Review Against Guidelines

#### Code Reads Like Prose
- Descriptive function and variable names — no abbreviations that require mental decoding
- Linear data flows — can you read top-to-bottom without jumping around?
- Efficient line count — no bloat, no unnecessary abstractions
- DRY — is anything duplicated that shouldn't be?
- Single responsibility — each function does ONE thing, each class has ONE purpose
- Testable — could you write a test for this without mocking half the system?

#### Make Invalid States Unrepresentable
- Constraints encoded in types, not runtime checks
- No scattered validation for the same invariant
- `std::optional`, enums, and constructors used to enforce validity

#### Trace the Data
- Where does each value come from? What constraints does it carry?
- Are there redundant conversions or unnecessary intermediates?
- Does every downstream consumer get what it expects?

#### Always Make It Better
- Did we touch code without improving it?
- Are there obvious improvements just outside the diff boundary? (note in suggestions, don't block)

#### Project Conventions (from CLAUDE.md)
- No docstrings unless asked
- No fallbacks — code works or fails loudly
- No dead code, no commented-out experiments
- No default arguments
- Leading underscores for class data members
- PascalCase functions, snake_case locals, kCamelCase constants
- "latest" not "last" for most recent values
- Parameter passing: pointer for mutation, const ref for read-only, const value for scalars

### 3. Check For Slop
- Comments that explain "what" instead of "why"
- Defensive checks for conditions that can't happen
- Unnecessary try/catch or error handling beyond system boundaries
- Verbose logging that doesn't match existing patterns
- Style inconsistencies with surrounding code

### 4. Present Results

```
## Review Summary

**Assessment**: [APPROVE / REQUEST CHANGES]

### Positive Findings
- What was done well

### Required Changes
- Issues that must be fixed (file:line references)

### Suggestions
- Optional improvements

### Convention Violations
- Any CLAUDE.md or guideline violations
```

Be specific with file:line references. Prioritize correctness and readability over micro-optimizations. If approved, suggest running `/validate-smol` next.

Base directory for this skill: /home/ubuntu/Documents/Github/smol/.claude/skills/validate-smol

# Validate smol

Run all automated checks for the smol flight controller. Activate `~/.venvs/smol` before every command.

## Checks

Run these in order. If a check fails, stop and report — do not continue to later checks.

### 1. Regenerate and format

Regenerate all generated files and run the formatter. This ensures we never commit stale generated code or unformatted source.

```bash
python3 protocol/generate.py
just format
```

Then verify the checks pass:

```bash
just check-format
just check-codegen
```

Both must pass. Generated files (`src/protocol/`) are excluded from formatting — the generator owns their style.

### 2. Native unit tests

```bash
just test-native
```

Report pass/fail count from the summary line (e.g., "118 test cases: 118 succeeded").

Known flaky: `test_smol_matches_full_after_full_sequence` (BUG-006, FullEkf nondeterminism). If ONLY this test fails, re-run once. If it fails twice, report it.

### 3. Thread sanitizer

```bash
just test-tsan
```

Catches data races in SharedState, ring buffer, and cross-thread communication. Requires `setarch -R` for ASLR compatibility on Linux 6.x.

### 4. Elixir GCS tests

```bash
just test-gcs
```

### 5. Native build

```bash
just build-native
```

### 6. RP2350B build (CMake)

```bash
just build-fc3
```

This catches missing source files in `CMakeLists.txt` and RP2350B-specific compilation errors that native builds miss.

### 7. Replay validation

```bash
just test-replay
```

This builds `native_full_ekf`, replays reference flight data through both EKFs, and checks RMS error bounds vs truth. Requires steps 4-5 to have passed.

## Report

```
## Validation Report

### Regenerate + format
[PASS — tree clean / PASS — N files updated / FAIL — details]

### Native tests
[PASS — N test cases: N succeeded / FAIL — details]

### Thread sanitizer
[PASS / FAIL — details]

### GCS tests
[PASS — N tests: N passed / FAIL — details]

### Native build
[PASS / FAIL]

### RP2350B build
[PASS / FAIL — details if failed]

### Replay validation
[PASS — N passed / FAIL — details]

### Summary
[READY TO SHIP / NEEDS FIXES — list what failed]
```

## Next Steps

- All pass: `/ship` to commit
- Failures: fix and re-run `/validate-smol`

# Plan Command

Plan a new feature or task with proper structure before implementation.

**Reference skills based on feature type:**
- API/backend: Read `.claude/skills/api-design-patterns/SKILL.md`
- React components: Read `.claude/skills/react-patterns/SKILL.md`
- UI styling: Read `.claude/skills/tailwind-conventions/SKILL.md`
- Error handling: Read `.claude/skills/error-handler/SKILL.md`
- TDD mode: Read `.claude/skills/test-generator/SKILL.md`

**For new projects:** Use `/greenfield` first to define specs, then `/plan` for implementation.

## Flags

- `--tdd` - Enable Test-Driven Development mode (write tests first)

## Validation

If no feature description provided, ask for one.

## Planning Steps

### 1. Gather Context (REQUIRED)

**You MUST read relevant files before creating a plan.** Don't plan based on assumptions.

Before planning:
- Read relevant CLAUDE.md files
- **Read the actual files** that will be modified
- Identify existing patterns and conventions
- Understand related code and dependencies

Use `Explore` agent or direct file reads to understand:
- Current implementation
- Existing patterns in similar code
- Test file locations and patterns

### 2. Requirements Clarification

Ask clarifying questions if needed:
- What is the expected behavior?
- What are the edge cases?
- What are the acceptance criteria?
- Are there performance requirements?

### 3. Create Plan

Structure the implementation with **specific details**:

**Detail Level Guidelines:**

| Change Type | Detail Level |
|-------------|--------------|
| Complex/risky changes | Line numbers + code snippets |
| Medium changes | Function/method names |
| Simple/obvious changes | File paths only |
| New files | File path + structure outline |

**Output Format:**
```
## Feature: [description]

### Requirements
- [ ] Requirement 1
- [ ] Requirement 2

### Technical Approach
1. Step 1 - [description]
   - Why: [reasoning for this approach]
2. Step 2 - [description]

### Files to Modify

#### `path/to/file.ts` (lines 45-67)
**Current:** [brief description of current state]
**Change:** [what will change]
```typescript
// Example of the change (for complex modifications)
function existingFunction() {
  // Add: new caching logic here
}
```

#### `path/to/new-file.ts` (NEW)
**Purpose:** [why this file is needed]
**Structure:**
- `functionA()` - [purpose]
- `functionB()` - [purpose]

### Dependencies
- [list any new dependencies]

### Testing Strategy
- Unit tests: [specific test cases]
- Integration tests: [approach]
- Test file: `path/to/tests/file.test.ts`

### Alternatives Considered
- [Alternative 1] - [why not chosen]

### Risks
- [potential issue] - [mitigation]

### Complexity
- [low/medium/high] - [justification]
```

### 4. TDD Mode (if --tdd flag)

When `--tdd` is specified, modify the plan to include:

```
### TDD Implementation Order

1. **Acceptance Criteria → Test Cases**
   - [ ] Test: [criteria 1 as test]
   - [ ] Test: [criteria 2 as test]

2. **Write Failing Tests First**
   Files to create/modify:
   - `__tests__/feature.test.ts` - [test descriptions]

3. **Implement to Pass Tests**
   - Implement minimum code to pass each test
   - Run tests after each change

4. **Refactor**
   - Clean up while keeping tests green
```

**TDD Workflow:**
```
Write test → Run (FAIL) → Implement → Run (PASS) → Refactor → Run (PASS)
```

### 5. Confidence Check

Run Pre-Implementation Confidence Check before proceeding.

### 6. Await Approval

Present plan and wait for user approval before implementation.

**Key review points for user:**
- Are the file changes correct?
- Is the approach sound?
- Any concerns about the changes?

## Example (Standard)

```
## Feature: Add rate limiting to API

### Requirements
- [ ] Limit requests to 100/minute per user
- [ ] Return 429 when exceeded
- [ ] Log rate limit hits

### Technical Approach
1. Add rate limiting middleware using existing Express pattern
   - Why: Consistent with authMiddleware.ts approach
2. Store counters in Redis (already used for sessions)

### Files to Modify

#### `src/middleware/rateLimitMiddleware.ts` (NEW)
**Purpose:** Rate limiting middleware
**Structure:**
- `rateLimiter()` - Express middleware
- `getRateKey()` - Generate Redis key

#### `src/app.ts` (line 23)
**Current:** Auth middleware only
**Change:** Add rate limiter after auth
```typescript
app.use(authMiddleware);
app.use(rateLimiter({ limit: 100, window: 60 })); // ADD
```

### Testing Strategy
- Unit tests: Mock Redis, test limit logic
- Integration tests: Hit endpoint 101 times
- Test file: `__tests__/middleware/rateLimitMiddleware.test.ts`

### Alternatives Considered
- express-rate-limit package - Adds dependency, we can do simpler

### Risks
- Redis connection issues - Fail open (allow requests)

### Complexity
- Medium - New middleware but follows existing patterns
```

## Example (TDD Mode)

```
/plan --tdd Add rate limiting to API
```

```
## Feature: Add rate limiting to API (TDD)

### TDD Implementation Order

1. **Acceptance Criteria → Test Cases**
   - [ ] Test: Returns 200 for requests under limit
   - [ ] Test: Returns 429 when limit exceeded
   - [ ] Test: Resets after window expires
   - [ ] Test: Different users have separate limits

2. **Write Failing Tests First**
   File: `__tests__/middleware/rateLimitMiddleware.test.ts`
   ```typescript
   describe('rateLimiter', () => {
     it('allows requests under limit', async () => { ... });
     it('returns 429 when limit exceeded', async () => { ... });
     it('resets after window expires', async () => { ... });
   });
   ```

3. **Implement to Pass Tests**
   - Create `rateLimitMiddleware.ts`
   - Implement `rateLimiter()` function
   - Run tests after each addition

4. **Refactor**
   - Extract Redis key generation
   - Add JSDoc comments
```

## Next Steps

After approval:
- If `--tdd`: Write tests first, then implement
- Otherwise: Start implementation
- Use `/review` for code review
- Use `/validate` to verify before completion
- Use `/ship` when ready to commit


ARGUMENTS: We need to work on BUG-007 in the backlog

---
